Raising Hands for Takbir: Positions for Men and Women
Commentary on sunnah of raising hands with proofs and women's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for raising hands during the opening takbir for men, slave women, and free women, and explain the evidence and the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
Men and slave women raise hands to ears; free women raise to shoulders due to awra.

The opening takbir (tahrimah) is the first sunnah of prayer. The Hanafi school specifies different hand positions based on the person's gender and status. This lesson explains these positions, their evidence from hadith, and why the free woman's position differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
Determine the hukm level of raising hands for the opening takbir. The text states it is Sunnah, meaning recommended but not obligatory.
Sunnah muakkadah according to the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the hadith evidence for men
The author cites multiple narrations from Wail ibn Hajar and Anas ibn Malik showing the Prophet raised his hands until his thumbs were opposite his ears. Identify the type of dalil (Sunnah ahad) and its implications.
The hadiths are considered sahih by Hakim and Daraqutni.
3
Note the ruling for slave women
The text explicitly states that a slave woman (amah) raises her hands to her ears like a man. Understand the reasoning: her forearms are not awra.
4
Understand the ruling for free women
The correct view (mufta bihi) is that a free woman raises her hands to her shoulders. The text mentions a counter-narration from Hasan but rejects it as less sound. The basis is her forearm being awra, necessitating modesty.
Some Hanafi scholars narrated an alternative but it is not the relied-upon position.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
There is a difference of opinion within the school: some narrations say free women raise to ears. Identify the tarjih mechanism (author says 'ala al-sahih') and why the shoulder position prevails.
The dispute is resolved by prioritizing concealment (satr) for the free woman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سنن الصلاة وهي إحدى وخمسون: رفع اليدين للتحريمة حذاءَ الأذنين للرّجلِ والأَمَةِ، وحذاءَ المَنْكِبَيْنِ للحرةِ، ونشر الأصابع، ومقارنة إحرام المقتدي لإحرام إمامه . فصل في سنن الصلاة (وهي إحدى وخمسون) تقريباً، منها أنه يسن: (رفع اليدين للتحريمة، حذاءَ الأذنين، للرجل) لما في صحيح مسلم عن وائل بن حجر أنه رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم رفع يديه حين دخل في الصلاة كـبر ووضعهما حيال أذنيه). ولما روى الطحاوي والدارقطني: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ) « إِذَا صَلَّى رَفَعَ يَدَيهِ حَتَّى يكونَ إبهامَاهُ حذاء أذُنَيْهِ ) (۳)، زاد الدارقطني فيه: « ثم لم يعد » . وروى هـو والحـاكـم عــن أنـس قال: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم « كبر فَحَاذَى بِإِبهَامِيهِ أذنيهِ ثُمَّ رَكَعَ حَتَّى اسْتَقَرَّ كُلِّ مِفْصَلٍ مِنْهُ وَانحَطَّ بالتكبير حتَّى سَبَقَتْ يَدَاهُ رُكْبَتَيْهِ » (۳). قال الحاكم: إسناده صحيح على شرط الشيخين. وروى الدارقطني بطريق آخر عن أنس قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ) إِذَا افْتَتَحَ الصَّلاةَ كَبَّرَ : ثم رفع يديه حتى يُحَاذِي بِإِبْهَامِيهِ أذنيه ثم يقول: سُبْحَانَكَ اللَّهمَّ وَبِحَمْدِكَ ) إلخ. وقال: رجال إسناده كلهم ثقات (وَ) حذاء أذني (الأمةِ)؛ لأنها كالرجل في الرفع وكالحرة في الركوع والسجود وتنضم لأن ذراعيها ليسا بعورة. (و) رفع اليدين ( حذاءَ المَنْكِبَيْنِ للحرّةِ على الصحيح، لأن مبنى حالها على الستر، وذراعها عورة، وهذه رواية محمد بن مقاتل عن أصحابنا، وفي المجتبى» إلى منكبيها حذاء ثدييها، واحترزنا بالصحيح عن رواية الحسن التي قدمناها أنها ترفع حذاء أذنيها.
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Prayer. They are approximately fifty-one: among them is that it is Sunnah: raising the hands for the takbir (opening proclamation) opposite the ears for the man, and opposite the shoulders for the free woman. [then the hadith evidence] ... (and) raising the hands opposite the shoulders for the free woman is the correct view, because her condition is based on concealment, and her forearm is ‘awra. This is the narration of Muhammad ibn Muqatil from our companions. In al-Mujtaba: to her shoulders opposite her breasts. And by 'correct' we guard against the narration of Hasan which we presented that she raises opposite her ears.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage discusses the Sunnah of raising the hands for the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah). The author begins by stating that this action is Sunnah, meaning it is recommended but not obligatory. He provides the specific positions: for men and slave women (amah), the hands are raised until the thumbs are opposite the ears. For a free woman, because her forearms are considered ‘awra, she should raise her hands only to her shoulders. The author cites several hadiths to support the position for men, including narrations from Wail ibn Hajar and Anas ibn Malik. He then notes that there is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: some narrate that a free woman also raises to her ears, but the correct (sahih) view is to the shoulders. This is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer; from the root h-r-m meaning to make forbidden (i.e., forbidden to engage in non-prayer actions).
حذاء الأذنين (hidha al-udhnayn): Opposite the ears; meaning the thumbs are aligned with the earlobes.
حذاء المنكبين (hidha al-mankibayn): Opposite the shoulders; meaning the palms are aligned with the tops of the shoulders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, to which level should a free woman raise her hands for the opening takbir?
A) To the ears
B) To the shoulders
C) To the chest
D) Above the head

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school differentiates hand raising for takbir based on gender and status; the free woman's awra dictates a lower position.

Sunnah of Spreading Fingers When Raising Hands
Commentary on the second sunnah: spreading fingers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct manner of spreading fingers during takbir and explain the evidence.

Core Idea
Spreading fingers moderately is Sunnah — not tight, not wide.

In this passage, the commentator explains the second Sunnah of raising hands: the position of the fingers. The proof is a hadith describing the Prophet's (PBUH) practice, and the commentary clarifies the exact manner: neither fully closed nor fully separated, but a natural moderate spread.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'nashr al-asabi' (spreading fingers) when raising hands for takbir. The ruling is Sunnah (specifically sunnah muakkadah).
Sunnah muakkadah is a confirmed recommended act; omitting it loses reward but does not affect validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a hadith: 'When he said the takbir, he would raise his hands spreading his fingers.'
This is an ahad hadith (single narrator chain) reported by Tirmidhi and Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The descriptive statement (fi'l) of the Prophet indicates a practice to be emulated. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions that are not specific to him are considered Sunnah.
This is not a command (amr) but an action; thus it establishes Sunnah, not obligation.
4
Note the proper manner
The commentary specifies moderation: 'la yadimm kull al-damm wa la yufarrij kull al-tafrij' — not fully closed nor fully separated.
This avoids extremes and ensures naturalness.
5
Consider the absence of ikhtilaf
The text indicates no dispute among schools on this point; it is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
There is no need for tarjih as all schools accept this Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ) يسن (نَشْرُ الأصابع) لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام « كَانَ إِذَا كَبَّرَ رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ نَاشِرَا أَصَابِعَهُ » ) وكيفيته أن لا يضم كل الضم ولا يفرج كل التفريج، بل يتركها على حالها منشورة
And it is Sunnah to spread the fingers, because it was narrated that the Prophet (PBUH) when he said the takbir would raise his hands, spreading his fingers. The manner is that he does not fully close nor fully separate, but leaves them in a natural spread state.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This short passage covers the second sunnah: spreading the fingers while raising the hands for the takbir. The author provides a hadith as proof. He then clarifies the proper manner: the fingers should not be tightly closed together nor spread wide apart, but moderately separated in a natural state.

Key Terms
نشر الأصابع (nashr al-asabi'): Spreading the fingers apart in a moderate, natural manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct way to spread the fingers when raising hands for takbir?
A) Fully separate all fingers
B) Fully close fingers together
C) Moderate spreading, not fully closed nor fully separated
D) Only spread the thumb and little finger

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah for finger position during raising hands is moderate spreading — not clenched nor fully splayed.

The Follower's Takbir: Simultaneous or After the Imam?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the follower's opening takbir should be simultaneous with the imam or immediately after

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the timing of the follower's takbir, and state the practical ruling (mufta bihi) on this issue.

Core Idea
The follower's takbir can be simultaneous or after; the ikhtilaf is over virtue, not validity.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the follower's opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) relative to the imam. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that simultaneity (muqaranah) is preferred, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue for immediate succession (ta'qib). The difference hinges on the interpretation of the Arabic particle 'fa' in the hadith 'When he makes takbir, then make takbir.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the ikhtilaf
Read the matn statement: 'It is Sunnah that the follower's opening takbir be simultaneous with the imam's.' Note that this is the view of Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn disagree, saying it should be after. Recognize that the disagreement is over virtue (awlawiyyah), not permissibility.
The matn itself presents Abu Hanifa's view as the Sunnah.
2
Analyze the linguistic argument of Abu Hanifa
Examine the hadith 'idha kabbara fakabbiru'. Abu Hanifa interprets 'idha' as indicating the same time, meaning 'when he makes takbir [at that time], then make takbir'. The word 'fa' here is argued to allow simultaneity (quran), as seen in the Quranic verse 7:204 where 'fa' in 'fastami'u' means listening during the recitation, not after.
The author cites Quran 7:204 to support this usage.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn argue that 'fa' primarily indicates immediate succession (ta'qib), so the follower should make takbir after the imam has finished his takbir. They rely on the common usage of 'fa'.
Both sides agree that the hadith is the proof; the difference is in the interpretation of the particle.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical effect: if the follower intends to do it after, his prayer is valid. But it is more virtuous to synchronize, as per Abu Hanifa's view, to avoid differing from the imam and to maintain harmony in congregation.
The author states 'la khilaf fi al-jawaz' (no dispute on permissibility).
5
Apply the ruling to an uncertain scenario
Read the discussion on uncertainty: if the follower thinks he made takbir before the imam, it does not count; if he thinks after or is unsure, it counts. A caution is given from al-Zuhayriyya that if there is any doubt, it is better to rule invalid as a precaution.
This part shows how the ruling is applied in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (مُقَارَنَةُ إِحْرَامِ المُقْتَدِي لإحْرَامِ إِمَامِهِ) عند الإمام؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر المؤتمين بالتكبير في زمــان يـكـبر فيه الإمام بقوله: « إذا كبر فكبروا ) ()، لأن إذا للوقت حقيقة كالحين، فيكون تقديره ره فكبروا في زمان . تكبير الإمام والفاء وإن كانت للتعقيب فقد تستعمل للقران كقوله : « وإذا قرأ فأنصتوا ، وكقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْهَانُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنصِتُوا ﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٠٤] يجب الاستماع والإنصات في زمان القراءة لا بعده. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : يكبر للتحريمة بعدما أحرم الإمام لما روينا والفاء للتعقيب. وعلمت الجواب بأن إذا للوقت والفاء تكون للقران ولا خلاف في الجواز عـلـى الصحيح، وإنما الخلاف في الأولوية، قال الإمام: الاقتداء عقد موافقة وإنها في القرا القران لا في ا التأخير، فكان أولى احترازاً عن الاختلاف المنهي عنه، وعندهما بعد إحرامه، لأن في القران احتمال وقوع التكبير سابقاً على تكبير الإمام، وهذا غير معتبر لأن كلامنا فيما إذا تيقن عدم السبق، فإن غـلـب عـلـى ظـنـه أنه كبر قبل الإمام لا يجزئه، وإن غلب على رواية أنه كبر بعد الإمام أو استوى الحــالان أجزأه لأن أمره محمول على الصواب حتى يظهر الخطأ، كما في ( التجنيس والمزيد »، ولكن في « الظهيرية » : إذا جازت الصلاة من وجه أو وجوه وفسدت من وجه فإنه يحكم بالفساد أخذاً بالتوفيق والاحتياط.
And it is Sunnah that the follower's opening takbir be simultaneous with the imam's opening takbir according to Abu Hanifa, because the Prophet ordered the followers to make takbir at the time the imam makes takbir by saying 'When he makes takbir, then make takbir.' Because 'idha' (when) denotes the time, so the meaning is 'make takbir in the time of the imam's takbir.' ... Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He says the takbir after the imam has entered into ihram, because 'fa' denotes immediate succession. ... The difference is only about preference (awlawiyyah).
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage addresses the third sunnah: the follower's opening takbir being simultaneous (muqaranah) with the imam's. The author presents the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, who relies on the hadith 'When he makes takbir, then make takbir.' Abu Hanifa argues that 'idha' indicates the same time, similar to the Quranic verse 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it' where listening must be during the recitation, not after. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that 'fa' indicates immediate sequence, so the follower should make takbir after the imam. The author clarifies that there is no disagreement about the permissibility; the difference is only about what is more virtuous (awlawiyyah). Abu Hanifa considers simultaneity more virtuous because it avoids the difference (ikhtilaf) that is prohibited in congregational prayer. The author also discusses the ruling if the follower is uncertain whether his takbir preceded the imam's: if he is certain it preceded, it does not count; if he thinks it was after or equal, it counts. However, the Zuhayriyya says that if the prayer is valid from one perspective but invalid from another, we rule it invalid as a precaution.

Key Terms
مقارنة إحرام المقتدي لإحرام إمامه (muqaranat ihram al-muqtadi li-ihram imamihi): The simultaneity of the follower's opening takbir with the imam's takbir.
القران (al-quran): In this context, it means simultaneity (that two actions occur at the same time), as opposed to 'ta'qib' (immediate succession).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence of the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the follower's takbir?
A) The prayer is invalid if the follower delays his takbir.
B) The follower's prayer is valid in both cases, but simultaneity is more virtuous.
C) The follower must repeat the prayer if he does not synchronize.
D) The imam's prayer is invalid if the follower delays.

Key Takeaway
The follower's takbir may be simultaneous or after the imam's; both are valid, but simultaneity is more virtuous to avoid ikhtilaf.

Placement of Hands: Right on Left Under the Navel
Commentary on the sunnah of placing hands after takbir, including the method and differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement in salah and describe the preferred method of grasping the wrist.

Core Idea
Placing the right hand on the left under the navel is Sunnah; the method combines both 'placing' and 'grasping' narrations.

After the opening takbir, the worshiper places his hands. This lesson explains the Hanafi position that it is Sunnah for men to place the right hand on the left under the navel, and details the method preferred by many mashayikh: grasping the wrist with the little finger and thumb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing the right hand on the left after the opening takbir. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, proven by the hadith 'min al-sunnah...'
Sunnah muakkadah is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith quoted: 'Inna min al-sunnah wada' al-yamin 'ala al-shimal tahta al-surrah.' This is an ahad hadith, so the ruling is sunnah, not fard.
The hadith is from Daraqutni; its chain is zanni al-thubut.
3
Describe the method
The method: place the palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, with the little finger and thumb circling the left wrist. This combines two narrations (placing and grasping).
Many mashayikh approved this because it acts by both hadiths.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi variation
There are other methods: placing palm on palm, or on the joint. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad had different preferences. The chosen method is the one that combines both hadiths.
The author quotes 'al-Mukhtar' as the relied-upon view.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school places hands on the chest, while Hanafi places under the navel. This is a valid ikhtilaf.
Women in Hanafi school place hands on their chest due to different ruling for 'awrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووَضعُ الرَّجُلِ يَدَهُ اليُمنى على اليُسرى تحت سُرَّتِهِ. وصفة الوضع أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كفّ اليُسرى، مُحَلِّقاً بالخِنْصَرِ والإبهام على الرَّسْغِ.. (و) يسن (وَضعُ الرَّجُلِ يَدَهُ اليُمنى على اليُسرى، تحت سُرَّتِهِ لحديث عليه: « إن من السنة وضع اليمين على الشَّمالِ تحت السُّرَّةِ » ) ولأنه أقرب إلى التعظيم، كما بين يدي الملوك، ووضعهما على العورة لا يضر فوق الثياب، وكذا بلا حائل؛ لأنها ليست لها حكم العورة في حقه، ولهذا تضع المرأة يديها على صدرها وهو عورة، (وصفة الوضع: أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى عـلـى ظـاهـر كـف اليُسرى، مُحَلِّقاً بالخِنْصَرِ والإبهام على الرُّسُغِ). واستحسنه كثير من مشايخنا، ليـكـون عـمـلاً بالحديثين لأنه ورد الأخذ، وورد الوضع وبالمذاهب احتياطاً لأنه قيل: يـضـع الـكـف عـلـى الـكـف، واختار بعضهم وضعها على المفصل. قال في «معراج الدراية » : كذا في « المجتبى» و« الظهيرية » و المبسوط » انتهى. وكذا قال صاحب ( المفيد » : يأخذ رسغ اليسرى بالخنصر والإبهام من اليمني، وهو المختار لأنه يلزم من الأخذ الوضع ولا ينعكس. وعن أبي يوسف: يقبض باليمنـى رســغ اليسرى واختاره الهندواني وقال محمد يضعها كذلك ويكون الرسغ وسط الكف كما في التبيين». وقيل: إن الذي استحسنه الكثير من الصفة المذكورة في المتن خارج عن المذاهب والأحاديث. انتهى. قلت: فعلى هذا ينبغي أن يفعل بصفة أحد الحديثين في وقت وبصفة الآخر في غيره، فيكون جامعاً بين المرويين حقيقة؛ لأن تلك الصفة ليس فيها حقيقة كل من المرويين تماماً
And regarding the placement of the hand: It is Sunnah for a man to place his right hand on his left under his navel. The description of the placement: He makes the palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, and he circles the little finger and thumb over the wrist. (and) it is Sunnah: placing the man's right hand on the left under his navel, because of the hadith: 'Indeed from the Sunnah is placing the right on the left under the navel.' And because it is closer to showing respect, like before kings. ... The description: he makes the palm of the right hand on the back of the left, circling the little finger and thumb on the wrist. Many of our masters have approved this, so that one acts by both hadiths (the hadith of placing and the hadith of grasping).
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage covers the fourth sunnah: after the takbir, the man places his right hand on his left under the navel. The author provides a hadith as proof and explains the rationale: it demonstrates humility and respect. The method preferred by many Hanafi scholars is to place the palm of the right hand on the back of the left, and to form a circle with the little finger and thumb around the left wrist. This combines two narrations: one about 'placing' and one about 'grasping.' There is some difference about the exact position: some say to place palm on palm, others on the joint. The author quotes from 'Miraj al-Diraya' and other sources, and notes that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad had different opinions. He concludes that it is best to occasionally practice one method and another to honor both hadiths.

Key Terms
الرسغ (al-rusgh): The wrist joint; the area where the hand meets the arm.
وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة (wada' al-yamin 'ala al-shimal tahta al-surrah): Placing the right hand on the left hand under the navel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the method of placing the right hand on the left that combines both 'placing' and 'grasping' narrations?
A) Palm on palm
B) Grasping the wrist with little finger and thumb
C) Placing palm on the chest
D) Interlocking fingers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that placing the right hand on the left under the navel is sunnah muakkadah, with the preferred method being to grasp the left wrist with the little finger and thumb.

Man's Hand Placement in Prayer (Hanafi Ruling)
Ruling on man's hand placement in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a man's hand placement during qiyam and describe the correct manner of placement.

Core Idea
A man places his right hand on his left under the navel, palm on back, encircling the wrist.

This lesson covers one of the most distinctive sunnah acts in the Hanafi prayer: the placement of hands during standing. The ruling is clear and specific, and understanding it correctly ensures that you follow the sunnah as transmitted by the Companions. Let's break down the matn from Nur al-Idah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the placement of the hands during qiyam (standing) in salah. In the Hanafi school, this is a sunnah muakkadah, not a pillar or wajib.
Sunnah muakkadah means highly recommended; leaving it is not sinful but loses reward.
2
Locate the position
The matn states the hands are placed 'under his navel' (tahta surratihi). This is the specific location for a man.
Contrast with the Shafi'i position of placing hands on the chest.
3
Describe the manner
The matn gives the detailed manner: the right palm is placed on the back of the left hand, and the little finger (khinsar) and thumb (ibham) encircle the wrist (rusgh).
The remaining fingers of the right hand are extended along the left forearm.
4
Memorize the ruling
This is a memorization anchor. Commit the exact wording to memory: position and manner.
Use the key terms surratihi and rusgh to recall the details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووَضعُ الرَّجُلِ يَدَهُ اليُمنى على اليُسرى تحت سُرِّتِهِ. وصفة الوضع أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كفّ اليُسرى، مُحَلِّقاً بالخِنْصَرِ والإبهام على الرَّسْغِ..
And the placement of the man's right hand on the left under his navel. The description of the placement is that he places the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, encircling with the little finger and thumb on the wrist.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This is the foundational matn ruling from Nur al-Idah regarding the sunnah placement of hands during standing in prayer. It states two things: (1) the place where hands are placed: under the navel, and (2) the manner of placement: the right palm on the back of the left hand, with the little finger and thumb encircling the wrist. This is the Hanafi position based on hadith.

Key Terms
سرته (surratihi): The navel; the location below which the man places his hands during qiyam in salah.
رسغ (rusgh): The wrist joint; the area where the hand meets the forearm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, where does a man place his hands during qiyam in salah?
A) On the chest
B) Under the navel
C) Above the navel
D) On the thighs

Key Takeaway
The sunnah for a man is to place his right hand on his left under the navel, with the right palm on the back of the left hand and the little finger and thumb encircling the wrist.

Timing of Follower's Takbir Relative to Imam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of the follower's takbir and evaluate the evidence from both sides.

Core Idea
The follower should say takbir with the imam to maintain compliance; delay is permissible but not optimal.

In congregational prayer, the timing of the follower's opening takbir relative to the imam is a subtle but important point. The Hanafi school has an internal debate: Abu Hanifa insists on simultaneity (qiran), while his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, prefer a slight delay (ta'qib). This lesson unpacks the linguistic and legal arguments behind each view, and clarifies that both are valid—the disagreement is about which is better, not about permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What exactly is being disputed? The timing of the follower's takbir tahrima relative to the imam's takbir.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa says the follower should say takbir simultaneously with the imam. He uses the Quranic verse 7:204, arguing that the letter fa' can indicate conjunction, and that following (iqtida') is a contract of compliance requiring simultaneity.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the follower should say takbir after the imam has finished. They argue that the primary meaning of fa' is sequence, and that this avoids any risk of preceding the imam.
4
Analyze the resolution
The text states there is no disagreement on permissibility—both timings yield a valid prayer. The difference is only about priority (awlawiyya). Abu Hanifa's view is considered better because it avoids the prohibited disagreement (ikhtilaf) in congregation.
5
Consider the ruling when timing is uncertain
If the follower is unsure whether he preceded the imam, his prayer is valid. Only if he is certain that he preceded does the prayer become invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكبير الإمام والفاء إن كانت للتعقيب فقد تستعمل للقران كقوله : « وإذا قرأ فأنصتوا ، وكقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْهَانُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنصِتُوا ﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٠٤] يجب الاستماع والإنصات في زمان القراءة لا بعده. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : يكبر للتحريمة بعدما أحرم الإمام لما روينا والفاء للتعقيب. وعلمت الجواب بأن إذا للوقت والفاء تكون للقران ولا خلاف في الجواز عـلـى الصحيح، وإنما الخلاف في الأولوية، قال الإمام: الاقتداء عقد موافقة وإنها في القرا القران لا في ا التأخير، فكان أولى احترازاً عن الاختلاف المنهي عنه، وعندهما بعد إحرامه، لأن في القران احتمال وقوع التكبير سابقاً على تكبير الإمام، وهذا غير معتبر لأن كلامنا فيما إذا تيقن عدم السبق، فإن غـلـب عـلـى ظنـه أنه كبر قبل الإمام لا يجزئه، وإن غلب على رواية أنه كبر بعد الإمام أو استوى الحــالان أجزأه لأن أمره محمول على الصواب حتى يظهر الخطأ، كما في ( التجنيس والمزيد »، ولكن في « الظهيرية » : إذا جازت الصلاة من وجه أو وجوه وفسدت من وجه فإنه يحكم بالفساد أخذاً بالتوفيق والاحتياط.
The takbir of the imam: And the letter fa' even if it is for sequence, it may be used for conjunction, as in his saying: 'And when he recites, listen' and as in the verse: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen and be silent' [7:204]. Listening and being silent are obligatory at the time of recitation, not after. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He says the tahrima takbir after the imam has entered ihram based on what we narrated, and the fa' is for sequence. You have learned the answer: that 'idha' is for time and the fa' is for conjunction. And there is no disagreement about permissibility according to the correct view; the difference is only about what is better. The Imam [Abu Hanifa] said: Following is a contract of compliance, and it is in conjunction, not in delay, so it is more appropriate to avoid the prohibited disagreement. According to them, after his ihram, because in conjunction there is the possibility of the takbir preceding the imam's takbir, but this is not considered because our discussion is when one is certain of non-precedence. If he strongly thinks he said it before the imam, it does not suffice; if he strongly thinks he said it after the imam or it is equal, it suffices because his action is considered correct until error appears, as in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. But in al-Zahiriyya: If the prayer is valid from one aspect and invalid from another, it is ruled invalid, taking caution.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the follower's takbir tahrima relative to the imam's. Abu Hanifa holds that the follower should say his takbir simultaneously with the imam's takbir (conjunction), based on the principle that following (iqtida') is a contract of compliance, and delaying would create a gap. He uses the analogy of the verse about listening during recitation, where the fa' indicates conjunction. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the follower should say takbir after the imam has completed his takbir (sequence), because the fa' primarily indicates sequence. The text explains that both are permissible, but the difference is about priority (awlawiyya). A further nuance: if the follower is uncertain about timing, his prayer is valid unless he is sure he preceded the imam. There is also a cautionary ruling from al-Zahiriyya that if there are mixed aspects, invalidity is assumed.

Key Terms
التعقيب (al-ta'qib): Sequential order; the letter fa' indicating that one action follows another without delay.
القران (al-qiran): Conjunction; doing two actions simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when should the follower say his takbir tahrima?
A) After the imam completes his takbir
B) At the same time as the imam
C) Before the imam
D) It doesn't matter

Key Takeaway
The follower's takbir should ideally be simultaneous with the imam's to maintain compliance, though a slight delay is permissible.

Man's Hand Placement in Salah: Proof and Description
Expanded hadith evidence and detailed grasp description for hand placement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling for a man's hand placement in salah, identify the hadith evidence, and describe the recommended Hanafi method while explaining the intra-madhhab variations.

Core Idea
A man's right hand on left under navel is sunnah; the encircling grasp combines two narrations.

This lesson examines the proof and detailed description of a man's hand placement in salah, a sunnah stressed by the Hanafi school. We begin with the hadith that establishes its practice, then explore the precise method recommended by the mashayikh, and finally understand the subtle differences among the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Evidence
Pinpoint the hukm (sunnah) and the dalil (hadith). The text explicitly says 'mina al-sunnah' and then cites the hadith text.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Analyze the Wisdom (Hikmah)
The author explains that this posture is closer to reverence, akin to standing before kings. Understand the rationale.
Also note the mention that placing hands on the private part (above garments) is not harmful.
3
Describe the Recommended Method
Read the description: palm of right on back of left, with little finger and thumb encircling the wrist. This is the method deemed good by many mashayikh.
This method is claimed to combine the two narrations: 'grasping' (akhdh) and 'placing' (wad').
4
Trace the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Compare the views of Abu Yusuf (grasps the wrist) and Muhammad (places palm on palm, with wrist at the middle of the hand). Note that the encircling method is the chosen view.
The author also suggests alternating between methods to act upon both narrations.
5
Synthesize the Concluding Recommendation
The author concludes that one can practice one description at one time and the other at another, or use the third composite method. The goal is to honor the varied transmissions.
This shows flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (وَضعُ الرَّجُلِ يَدَهُ اليُمنى على اليُسرى، تحت سُرَّتِهِ لحديث عليه: « إن من السنة وضع اليمين على الشَّمالِ تحت السُّرَّةِ » ) ولأنه أقرب إلى التعظيم، كما بين يدي الملوك، ووضعهما على العورة لا يضر فوق الثياب، وكذا بلا حائل؛ لأنها ليست لها حكم العورة في حقه، ولهذا تضع المرأة يديها على صدرها وهو عورة، (وصفة الوضع: أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى عـلـى ظـاهـر كـف اليُسرى، مُحَلِّقاً بالخِنْصَرِ والإبهام على الرُّسُغِ). واستحسنه كثير من مشايخنا، ليـكـون عـمـلاً بالحديثين لأنه ورد الأخذ، وورد الوضع وبالمذاهب احتياطاً لأنه قيل: يـضـع الـكـف عـلـى الـكـف، واختار بعضهم وضعها على المفصل. قال في «معراج الدراية » : كذا في « المجتبى» و« الظهيرية » و المبسوط » انتهى. وكذا قال صاحب ( المفيد » : يأخذ رسغ اليسرى بالخنصر والإبهام من اليمني، وهو المختار لأنه يلزم من الأخذ الوضع ولا ينعكس. وعن أبي يوسف: يقبض باليمنـى رســغ اليسرى واختاره الهندواني وقال محمد يضعها كذلك ويكون الرسغ وسط الكف كما في التبيين». وقيل: إن الذي استحسنه الكثير من الصفة المذكورة في المتن خارج عن المذاهب والأحاديث. انتهى. قلت: فعلى هذا ينبغي أن يفعل بصفة أحد الحديثين في وقت وبصفة الآخر في غيره، فيكون جامعاً بين المرويين حقيقة؛ لأن تلك الصفة ليس فيها حقيقة كل من المرويين تماماً بل صفة ثالثة فيها جمع لهما لا على وجه التمام لكل منهما. انتهى.
And it is sunnah (the placement of the man's right hand on the left under his navel) due to the hadith: 'Indeed from the sunnah is to place the right on the left under the navel.' And because it is closer to reverence, as in the presence of kings. And placing them on the private part does not harm if above garments, and likewise without a barrier, because it does not have the ruling of a private part for him. For this reason, a woman places her hands on her chest, which is a private part. (And the description of placement: that he places the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, encircling with the little finger and thumb on the wrist.) And many of our mashayikh deemed this good, so that it acts upon both hadith, because there is a narration of 'grasping' and a narration of 'placing' and as a precaution between the schools, because it is said: he places the palm on the palm. And some chose placing on the wrist. He said in Mirqat al-Diraya: 'Thus in al-Mujtaba, al-Zahiriyya, and al-Mabsut.' End. And likewise the author of al-Mufid said: 'He takes the left wrist with the little finger and thumb of the right, and it is chosen because grasping necessarily entails placing, but not vice versa.' And from Abu Yusuf: 'He grasps the left wrist with the right hand,' and al-Hindwani chose that. And Muhammad said: 'He places them likewise, and the wrist is in the middle of the hand.' As in al-Tabyin. And it is said: That which many deemed good of the mentioned description in the matn is outside the schools and hadith. End. I say: Based on this, one should practice one description at one time and the other at another time, thus truly combining the two narrations, because that description does not contain the reality of each narration completely, but rather a third description combining them without perfection for each. End.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This section expands on the matn ruling with hadith evidence: a hadith states that placing the right hand on the left under the navel is sunnah. The author explains the wisdom: it is a posture of reverence. He addresses a point about uncovering the private part: if the hands are placed over garments, it is fine. The description of the grasp is detailed: the right palm on the back of the left, with the little finger and thumb encircling the wrist (like a ring). Many scholars preferred this because it combines the two narrations: one mentions 'grasping' (akhdh) and the other 'placing' (wad'). The text then presents a dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad have slightly different descriptions. The author concludes that one can alternate between methods to practice both hadiths. The final point is that the commonly recommended description is a third way that combines both narrations but is not perfect for either.

Key Terms
تحليقاً (tahlīqan): Encircling; making a ring shape with the little finger and thumb around the wrist.
الرسغ (al-rusgh): The wrist joint.
الأخذ (al-akhdh): Grasping; one of the two narrated actions for hand placement.
الوضع (al-wad'): Placing; the other narrated action for hand placement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence cited in this passage for the sunnah of a man placing his right hand on his left under the navel?
A) A Quranic verse
B) A hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him)
C) Consensus (ijma')
D) Analogical reasoning (qiyas)

Key Takeaway
A man's hand placement in salah is a sunnah based on a direct hadith, with the recommended method being to encircle the left wrist with the thumb and little finger of the right hand, though other methods are permissible.

Woman's Hand Placement in Salah
Ruling on woman's hand placement with proof of modesty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a woman's hand placement during qiyam and explain the reason for the difference from men.

Core Idea
A woman places her hands on her chest without encircling for greater modesty.

A key difference between men and women in salah is hand placement. This lesson derives the Hanafi ruling from the Nur al-Idah text, emphasizing the underlying reason of modesty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hand placement during qiyam. The text says 'يسن' indicating it is sunnah (recommended).
Sunnah here means recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the method
The woman places her hands on her chest (صدرها). The phrase 'من غير تحليق' explicitly excludes the encircling grip (tahliq) used by men.
Tahliq is the act of encircling the wrist with thumb and little finger.
3
Understand the proof
The reason given is 'لأنه أستر لها' (because it is more concealing for her). This connects the ruling to the principle of modesty.
The chest is part of a woman's awrah, so covering it is recommended.
4
Contrast with men
Men place hands under the navel and perform tahliq. Women differ to maximize concealment.
This contrast highlights that rulings may differ based on gender due to different awrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (وَضعُ المرأةِ يَدَيْها على صدرها من غير تحليق لأنه أستر لها.
And it is sunnah (the placement of the woman's hands on her chest without encircling because it is more concealing for her).
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This is the ruling for women: they place their hands on their chest (over the breasts) without the encircling grip (tahliq) that men do. The reason given is modesty ('astar), as the chest is an 'awrah for women. This contrasts with men, who place hands under the navel. The 'encircling' (tahliq) is specific to men's hand placement.

Key Terms
تحليق (tahlīq): Encircling the wrist with the little finger and thumb; men's method of hand placement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why do women place their hands on their chest without tahliq?
A) Because it is more comfortable
B) Because it is more concealing (astar)
C) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) specifically commanded it
D) Because they cannot do tahliq

Key Takeaway
A woman's hand placement in salah is on her chest without encircling, based on the principle of modesty.

Thana in Salah: Sunnah Not Obligatory
Ruling on thana after takbir tahrima

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of thana and explain the hadith evidence that supports its sunnah status.

Core Idea
Thana is sunnah; the takbir alone suffices without it.

The thana is the opening supplication recited after the takbir tahrima. In this passage, the author unequivocally states it is sunnah and provides a hadith from al-Tabarani to support this. The hadith also clarifies that omitting thana does not affect the validity of the prayer, reinforcing its recommended nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states 'وَ) يسن (الثَّناءُ)' — 'and it is sunnah (the thana)'. So the act is reciting thana after takbir tahrima, and the ruling is sunnah (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites a hadith: 'إذا قُمتُم إلى الصلاةِ فَارْفَعُوا أَيْدِيكُمْ ... ثم قُولوا: سبحانَكَ اللهم وبحمدك ... وإِنْ لم تَزيدُوا على التكبير أجزأكُم'. This is from al-Tabarani.
The hadith includes both the command to say thana and the statement that only takbir suffices.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
The command to say thana indicates it is prescribed, but the clause 'if you do not add more than the takbir, it suffices you' shows it is not obligatory. In Hanafi usul, a command without a qarinah (indication) of obligation indicates nadb (recommendation) when accompanied by a concession.
Thus, the hadith itself indicates sunnah, not wajib.
4
Note any ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf within or outside the Hanafi school; all schools regard thana as sunnah.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a person should recite thana, but if they omit it, the salah remains valid. The sunnah is to recite it, and there is no compensation required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن (الثَّناءُ) لما روينا ) ولقوله : « إذا قُمْتُم إلى الصَّلاةِ فَارْفَعُوا أَيْدِيكُمْ ولا تُخالف آذانكم ثم قُولوا: سبحانَكَ اللهم وبحمدك وتَبَارَكَ اسْمُكَ وَتَعَالَى جدَّك ولا إِلَهَ غَيْرُكَ، وإِنْ لم تَزيدُوا على التكبير أجزأكُم ). رواه الطبراني وسنذكر معاني ألفاظـه إن شاء الله تعالى
And it is sunnah (the thana) due to what we narrated and due to his saying: 'When you stand for prayer, raise your hands and do not lift them above your ears, then say: Glory be to You, O Allah, and with Your praise, blessed is Your name, exalted is Your majesty, there is no god but You. And if you do not add more than the takbir, it suffices you.' Narrated by al-Tabarani. We will mention the meanings of its words if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
The thana is the opening supplication recited after the takbir tahrima. The text states it is sunnah and provides a hadith from al-Tabarani with specific wording. The hadith indicates that if one only says the takbir without any thana, it suffices, but the sunnah is to recite it. The author promises to explain the meanings of the words later.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening supplication in salah recited after takbir, praising Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on reciting thana after takbir?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Thana is a sunnah act in salah; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.

The Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ta'awwudh in Salah
Ruling on ta'awwudh and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding ta'awwudh and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is a sunnah of the prayer itself; the follower also says it.

The ta'awwudh (saying 'I seek refuge in Allah from Shaytan') is a sunnah before recitation in salah. But who should say it? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it dependent on recitation, while Abu Yusuf argues it is a sunnah of the prayer. Later authorities sided with Abu Yusuf. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its variant
Identify the two views within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (ta'awwudh is for recitation) versus Abu Yusuf (ta'awwudh is for the prayer).
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Follow Abu Yusuf's reasoning: the need for refuge from Shaytan applies to the entire prayer, not just recitation; thus the follower, who prays, should also say ta'awwudh.
He uses qiyas and the hadith of Abu Sa'id.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The text states that in al-Khulasa and al-Dhakhira, Abu Yusuf's view is considered correct (sahih). This becomes the mufta bihi.
The 'apparent madhhab' was Abu Hanifa's, but later tarjih changed.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Abu Yusuf, the follower (muqtadi) also says ta'awwudh silently; according to Abu Hanifa, he does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن (التَّعوذُ ) فيقول: أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم، وهو ظاهر المذهب واختاره شمس الأئمة، وأبو عمرو، وعاصم، وابن كثير من القراء، أو يقول: أستعيذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم، واختاره الهندواني ومن القراء حمزة لموافقته القرآن وحديث أبي سعيد أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كـان إذا قام إلى الصلاة استفتح ثم يقول: « أعوذُ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم » (٣) وقوله: (للقراءة) فيها إشارة إلى أن من لا يقرأ لا يتعوذ، لأنه تابع للقراءة فيأتي به المسبوق، كالإمام د لا المقتدي، لأنه لا يقرأ والأمر بها معلّق بإرادة القراءة، وهذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد، ويجعل أبو يوسف الاستعاذة تبعاً للثناء سنة للصلاة؛ لأنها لدفع وسوسة الشيطان والمصلي أحــوج إليه من القارئ فيلحق به دلالة، قال في «الخلاصة » و « الذخيرة : قول أبي يوسف الصحيح.
And it is sunnah (the ta'awwudh). So he says: 'I seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Shaytan.' And this is the apparent madhhab, chosen by Shams al-A'imma, Abu 'Amr, 'Asim, and Ibn Kathir among the reciters. Or he says: 'I seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Shaytan,' chosen by al-Hindwani and among the reciters Hamzah, because it agrees with the Quran and the hadith of Abu Sa'id that the Prophet, when he stood for prayer, would open then say: 'I seek refuge in Allah the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing from the accursed Shaytan.' And his saying: (for recitation) indicates that one who does not recite does not seek refuge, because it is dependent on recitation. So the latecomer (masbuq) says it, like the imam, but not the follower (muqtadi), because he does not recite, and the command is attached to the intention of recitation. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf considers the ta'awwudh as following the thana, a sunnah of the prayer, because it is to repel the whisperings of the Shaytan, and the praying person is more in need of it than the reciter, so it is analogically attached. He said in al-Khulasa and al-Dhakhira: The saying of Abu Yusuf is correct.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage covers the ta'awwudh (saying 'I seek refuge in Allah from Shaytan') before recitation in salah. Two wordings are mentioned. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the ta'awwudh is for recitation only; thus, those who do not recite (like a follower) do not say it. However, the latecomer (masbuq) who will recite does say it. Abu Yusuf holds that ta'awwudh is a sunnah of the prayer itself, independent of recitation, because the need for refuge from Shaytan is for the prayer overall. The text notes that the view of Abu Yusuf is considered correct in al-Khulasa and al-Dhakhira. This affects whether a follower (muqtadi) should say it; according to the preferred view, he should.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The act of seeking refuge in Allah from Shaytan before recitation.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has started but will later complete missed rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, who should say the ta'awwudh?
A) Only the imam
B) Only those who recite (imam and latecomer)
C) Everyone, including the follower
D) Only the individual praying alone

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that ta'awwudh is a sunnah of the prayer, so the follower also says it.

Tasmiyah at the Beginning of Each Rak'ah
Ruling on saying basmalah before fatihah in each rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting tasmiyah before al-Fatihah in each rak'ah and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Tasmiyah is a sunnah before fatihah in every rak'ah, not wajib nor part of the surah.

This lesson addresses whether the basmalah is recited before al-Fatihah in prayer. The Hanafi school holds it is sunnah, supported by multiple hadith. We will examine the evidence and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before reciting al-Fatihah in prayer. The ruling is sunnah (tusannu), not wajib or fard.
The text explicitly uses 'tusannu' (it is sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites hadith from Ibn 'Abbas, Umm Salamah, and Abu Hurayrah. These are ahad hadith (non-mutawatir) but sufficient for establishing a sunnah.
The dalil is from the Prophet's action and statements.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent practice of opening prayer with basmalah indicates it is a recommended act. It does not prove obligation because the action is not accompanied by a command implying wujub.
Hanafi usul: amr (command) indicates wujub, but here it is an action, not a command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers basmalah part of al-Fatihah itself and recites it aloud in some prayers. They also cite Umm Salamah's hadith.
The disagreement is about both the nature and the ruling of basmalah in prayer.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the fact that basmalah was revealed for separation between surahs, as stated by the text. The hadith of Abu Hurayrah shows the Prophet did not count it as part of al-Fatihah.
The mufta bihi position is that tasmiyah is sunnah and recited silently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) تسن ( التسميةُ أول كلِّ ركعة) وهي آية من القرآن أنزلت للفصل بين السور على الأصح، ليست من الفاتحة ولا من كل سورة يسن الإتيان بها في ابتداء القراءة قبل الفاتحة لقول ابن عباس : كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم « يَفْتَتِحُ صلاته ببسم الله الرّحمنِ الرَّحيمِ ) وقول أم سلمة : ( أنَّ النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَرَأَ بِسمِ ا الرحمنِ الرَّحيمِ في الفَاتِحَةِ فِي الصَّلاةِ وعدها آية ). ذكره النووي والحاكم وقول نعيم: ( صليتُ خَلْفَ أَبِي هُرَيْرَة فقرأ بسمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمنِ الرَّحيمِ ثمَّ قَرَأَ بِأم القرآنِ فلما سلم قال: والذي نفسي بيده إني لأشبَهَكُم صَلاةٌ بِرَسُولِ اللهِ » (۳). رواه ابن حبان وابن خزيمة في صحيحهما ورواه الطحاوي وزاد: والمنفرد
And it is sunnah (the tasmiyah at the beginning of every rak'ah). And it is a verse of the Quran revealed for separation between surahs, according to the most correct view. It is not part of al-Fatihah nor of any surah. It is sunnah to recite it at the start of recitation before al-Fatihah due to the saying of Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Prophet used to open his prayer with 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim.'' And the saying of Umm Salamah: 'The Prophet recited 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' in al-Fatihah in prayer and counted it as a verse.' Mentioned by al-Nawawi and al-Hakim. And the saying of Nu'aym: 'I prayed behind Abu Hurayrah, and he recited 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' then recited Umm al-Quran (al-Fatihah). When he said salam, he said: 'By the One in Whose hand is my soul, I am the most similar of you to the prayer of the Messenger of Allah.' Narrated by Ibn Hibban and Ibn Khuzaymah in their Sahihs, and by al-Tahawi, and he added: 'and the one praying alone.'
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This ruling states that it is sunnah to say 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' at the beginning of each rak'ah before reciting al-Fatihah. The text clarifies that the basmalah is a verse of the Quran used to separate surahs; it is not part of al-Fatihah itself nor of any other surah. Evidence is provided from hadith: Ibn 'Abbas reports that the Prophet opened his prayer with basmalah; Umm Salamah reports that he recited it in al-Fatihah and considered it a verse; and a narration from Abu Hurayrah shows he recited it before al-Fatihah. This supports the Hanafi practice of reciting basmalah silently before al-Fatihah in each rak'ah.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where is the basmalah recited in salah?
A) Only before the first surah after fatihah
B) At the beginning of each rak'ah before fatihah
C) Only in the first rak'ah
D) It is not recited at all

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, saying 'Bismillah' before al-Fatihah is a sunnah act in every rak'ah, not a pillar or a wajib.

Is Basmalah in Prayer Wajib or Sunnah? The Hanafi Position
Expanding the ruling on basmalah in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on basmalah in prayer and explain why the majority of later Hanafis considered it sunnah despite early opinions of wajib.

Core Idea
Basmalah in prayer is sunnah, not wajib; omitting it does not require Sujud al-Sahw.

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Is saying 'Bismillah' before al-Fatihah in prayer wajib or sunnah? The text presents multiple views from early Hanafi authorities, including statements attributed to Abu Hanifa himself, and then explains why the later relied-upon position is sunnah. You will learn to distinguish between the different opinions, evaluate the evidence, and apply the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the final relied-upon ruling in the school? Identify it as sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
This is the mufta bihi for fatwa.
2
Identify the opposing view
Who held that basmalah is wajib? List the early Hanafis (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, some narrations from Abu Hanifa) and the Karabisiyyah.
Note that the dispute is internal to the school.
3
Follow the evidence for both sides
What proof does each side cite? The wajib side likely relies on general commands; the sunnah side relies on the hadith from Anas that the Prophet and caliphs did not recite it aloud.
The hadith is from Muslim and is the key dalil.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How do Hanafi scholars explain the hadith? They say it only negates audible recitation, not recitation itself; but they still conclude it is sunnah because the practice was not to recite it aloud.
The word 'wajib' in some references is reinterpreted as 'confirmed' (thubut).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which view is operative for fatwa today? The majority of later Hanafis (al-Kasani, al-Razi, al-Samdasi) hold it sunnah, no Sujud al-Sahw.
Authorities like al-Bahr and al-Khulasah confirm this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعدما شرح الزيلعي هذا المحل على أنها سُنَّة قال: في بــاب سجود السهو . ومنها أي واجبات الصلاة ،البسملة، فإذا تركها يجب عليه سجود السهو وقيل: لا يجب وقيل: إن تركها قبل الفاتحة تجب، وإن تركها بين الفاتحة والسورة لا تجب. انتهى كلامه. وقال العلامة الشيخ علي المقدسي في شرحه نظم ( الكنز ) عن المجتبى ) الصحيح أنها تجب في كل ركعة. قال شيخنا شيخ الإسلام السمديسي في شرح المختار » : ليست بواجبة فقد حكى المحققون من الحنفية كالإمام أبي بكر الرازي والعلامة أبي بكر الكاساني وغيرهما: الخلاف بين أئمتنا في السنية لا في الوجوب. قال بعض المحققين القول بالوجوب ليس له أصل في الرواية، وما نسب إلى أبي حنيفة من الخلاف في الوجوب فهو من طغيان اليراع، ومن نسب إليه القول بالوجوب فليس بمشهور الاختيار كمحمد بن القاسم الخوميني و البرهان الكافي وغيرهما. وصرح صاحب ( الخلاصة» بعدم سجود السهو بتركها انتهى. ولكن في ( الغاية » أوجب عين الأئمة الكرابيسي السهو بترك البسملة بين الفاتحة والسورة، وأيضاً قال في معراج الدراية : الخلاف في الوجوب أي: وجوب البسملة، فعندهمـا ورواية المعلى عن أبي حنيفة أنها تجب في الثانية كوجوبها في الأولى. وفي رواية الحسـن عــن أبـي حنيفة أنها لا تجب إلا عند افتتاح الصلاة، وإن قرأها في غيره فحسن، والصحيح أنـهـا تجـب فـي كـل ركعة حتى لو سها عنها قبل الفاتحة يلزمه السهو وكذا قال ابن وهبان في نظمه: ولو لم يبسمل ساهياً كل ركعـــة يسجد إذ بوجوبها قال الأكثر (٢) ولكن لم يسلم دعواه الأكثرية. وقال في ( البحر » : وهذا أي: القول بالوجوب كله ضعیف، والمواظبة عليها لم تثبت لما في مسلم عن أنس : صليت خلف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر وعمر « وعثمان فلم اسمع منهم أحداً يقول: بسم الله الرّحمن الرّحيم ) وإن كان قد أجاب عنه أئمتنا بأنه لم يرد نفي القراءة بــل السماع للإخفاء، بدليل ما رواه الجماعة « فكانوا لا يجهرون ببسم الله الرَّحمنِ الرَّحيمِ» وهو دليلنا على الإخفاء ولولا التصريح بلزوم السهو بتركها لقلت: إن الوجوب في كلامهم بمعنى الثبوت انتهى.
And after al-Zayla'i explained this matter as sunnah, he said: In the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw. Among them (i.e., the wajibat of prayer) is basmalah. If one omits it, Sujud al-Sahw is obligatory. It is said: not obligatory. And it is said: if he omits it before Fatihah, it is obligatory; if he omits it between Fatihah and the surah, it is not obligatory. End of his words. And Allamah Shaykh Ali al-Maqdisi said in his commentary on the versification of al-Kanz from al-Mujtaba: The correct view is that it is obligatory in every rak'ah. Our teacher Shaykh al-Islam al-Samdasi said in Sharh al-Mukhtar: It is not obligatory, for the verifiers from the Hanafis such as Imam Abu Bakr al-Razi and Allamah Abu Bakr al-Kasani and others have reported that the disagreement among our imams is about sunnah, not obligation. Some verifiers said the statement of obligation has no basis in narration, and what is attributed to Abu Hanifah of disagreement in obligation is from the tyranny of the pen, and whoever attributes to him the statement of obligation is not of well-known choice, like Muhammad ibn al-Qasim al-Khumayni and al-Burhan al-Kafi and others. And the author of al-Khulasah explicitly stated the absence of Sujud al-Sahw for omitting it. End. But in al-Ghayah, the core of the Karabisiyyah imams obligated Sujud al-Sahw for omitting basmalah between Fatihah and surah. Also, he said in Ma'arij al-Dirayah: The disagreement is about obligation, i.e., obligation of basmalah. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the narration of al-Mu'alla from Abu Hanifah, it is obligatory in the second as in the first. In the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifah, it is only obligatory at the opening of prayer, and if he recites it elsewhere, it is good. The correct view is that it is obligatory in every rak'ah, such that if he forgets it before Fatihah, Sujud al-Sahw is required. Similarly, Ibn Wahban said in his versification: 'And if he does not say basmalah forgetfully in every rak'ah, he prostrates because the majority said it is obligatory.' But his claim of majority is not secure. And he said in al-Bahr: This, i.e., the statement of obligation, is all weak, and constancy upon it is not established because of what is in Muslim from Anas: I prayed behind the Prophet (peace be upon him), Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and I did not hear any of them say 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. Although our imams responded to it by saying that he did not negate recitation but rather hearing due to concealment, as evidence of what the group narrated: 'They would not recite Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim aloud.' And it is our evidence for concealment. And were it not for the explicit statement of the necessity of Sujud al-Sahw for omitting it, I would have said: The obligation in their speech means confirmation. End.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of basmalah in prayer. The author discusses multiple opinions: whether basmalah is wajib or sunnah, and whether omitting it requires Sujud al-Sahw. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that basmalah is sunnah, not wajib, and thus its omission does not necessitate Sujud al-Sahw. This is supported by the hadith from Anas that the Prophet and caliphs did not recite it aloud, indicating concealment, and by the statements of later Hanafi authorities. The passage also notes that some early scholars, like the Karabisiyyah, held it wajib between Fatihah and surah, but the majority of the school consider this weak. The author concludes that the strongest view is that basmalah is sunnah, and the term 'wajib' in some statements is interpreted as 'confirmed' (thubut) rather than legally obligatory.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmalah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before reciting the Fatihah in prayer.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed for unintentional omissions or additions in prayer.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; here disputed whether it means legal obligation or confirmation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling regarding basmalah in prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is wajib, and omitting it requires Sujud al-Sahw.
B) It is sunnah, and omitting it does not require Sujud al-Sahw.
C) It is fard, and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
D) It is haram to recite aloud.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that basmalah before al-Fatihah in prayer is sunnah, and omitting it does not invalidate the prayer nor require Sujud al-Sahw.

Ruling on Saying Ameen After Al-Fatihah
Stating the ruling and linguistic derivation of Ameen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying Ameen in prayer, explain its proof from hadith, and distinguish it from Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Ameen is a sunnah du'a, not Quran; its reward requires sincerity, not precise timing.

Ameen is a common utterance in prayer, but its legal status and meaning are often misunderstood. This lesson clarifies that the Hanafi school considers it a recommended sunnah, supported by prophetic hadith, and emphasizes that it is not part of the Quran. We will also explore its linguistic roots and the conditions for receiving forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is 'al-ta'min' (saying Ameen). According to the passage, it is sunnah for the imam, the follower, and the one praying alone. Also sunnah for a reciter outside prayer.
Sunnah here means recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'When the imam says Ameen, say Ameen, for whoever's Ameen coincides with the angels' Ameen, his previous sins are forgiven.' This hadith is agreed upon (Bukhari and Muslim).
The passage also mentions other narrations that include the one praying alone.
3
Interpret the condition of reward
The 'coincidence' mentioned in the hadith is interpreted by scholars as sincerity and trust in Allah, not necessarily uttering Ameen at the exact same moment as the angels.
This avoids an impossible condition.
4
Confirm the non-Quranic status
Ameen is not part of the Quran because it is not written in the mus'haf. The passage states that claiming it is from the Quran constitutes apostasy, showing scholarly consensus on this point.
This is agreed upon by all schools.
5
Explore the linguistic derivation
Ameen originates from 'Ya Ameen' (O Responder), a name of Allah. The vocative was dropped and the alif lengthened. It means 'respond' or 'do'. The Prophet taught it as a seal on al-Fatihah.
Four pronunciations exist; the most common is with madd and takhfeed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ) يسن ( التَّأمينُ) للإمام والمأموم والمنفرد، لقوله : « إذا أمَّنَ الإمامُ فأمنُوا فَإِنَّهُ مَنْ وَافَقَ تَأمِينُهُ تأمين الملائكةِ غفر له ما تقدَّم من ذنبه ) متفق عليه زاد في مجمع الروايات وما تأخر، والمراد من الموافقة الإخلاص، والثقة بالله تعالى، لا الموافقة في التلفظ بها في وقت واحد. قال الأزهري غفر له دعا له، وغفره دعا عليه، لأن الغـفـر هـو : الاعدام، انتهـى مـن المستصفى» و«الدراية». وفي رواية للبخاري : « إذا قال الإمام غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين قولوا: آمين )، الحديث، وفي مسلم: « إِذَا قَالَ أحدكم في الصَّلاةِ آمينَ» (۳) الحديث، قــال عـبـد الـحـق: في هذه الرواية اندرج المنفرد، وفي « الكشاف » روى عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: « لقننـي جبرائيل عليه الصلاة والسلام عندَ فَراغِي مِنَ الفَاتِحَةِ آمين وقال : إِنَّهُ كالختم على الكِتَابِ ) وليس من القرآن بدليل أنه لم يثبت في المصاحف، وفي المجتبى» لا خلاف أن آمين ليس من القرآن، حتّى قالوا بارتداد مـــن قــال أنـه من القرآن، وأنه مسنون في حق المنفرد والإمام والمأموم والقارئ خارج الصلاة، وفي آمين أربع لغات أفصحن وأشهرةً بالمد والتخفيف؛ لأن أصله يا أمين استجب دعانا، وهو اسم من أسماء الله تعالى، إلا أنه أسقط بالنداء فأقيم المد مقامه، والمعنى: استجب، وهو : صوت سُمي به الفعل الذي هو استجب، وعـــن ابن عباس سألت رسول الله : ( عَنْ مَعْنَى آمین فقال: افعل ) وقیل: تعريب هيمن أي: هيمن مي خواهم أو هيمن مي بايد. قال الشاعر : [من البسيط] : يا رب إنك ذو مـــن ومغفـــــرة ثبت بعافية ليل المحبينا يارب لا تسلبني حبها أبداً ويرحم الله عبداً قـــــال: آمينــــا (۱) والثانية بقصر الألف والتخفيف كما قال الشاعر : [من الطويل] تباعد عني فطحل إن دعوتــــه أمين فزاد الله ما بيننا(۷)
And it is sunnah (to say Ameen) for the imam, follower, and one praying alone, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'When the imam says Ameen, say Ameen, for whoever's Ameen coincides with the Ameen of the angels, his previous sins will be forgiven.' Agreed upon. Added in Majma' al-Riwayat: 'and later sins.' The intended meaning of 'coincidence' is sincerity and trust in Allah, not coinciding in uttering at the same time. Al-Azhari said: 'Ghafara lahu' means prayed for him; 'Ghafarahu' means supplicated against him, because al-ghafr is destruction. End from al-Mustasfa and al-Dirayah. In a narration of al-Bukhari: 'When the imam says 'Ghayri al-maghdubi alayhim wa la al-dallin', say Ameen.' The hadith. And in Muslim: 'When one of you says in prayer Ameen...' the hadith. Abd al-Haq said: In this narration, the one praying alone is included. In al-Kashshaf, it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Jibril taught me to say Ameen after finishing al-Fatihah and said: It is like a seal on the book.' And it is not from the Quran, as evidenced by its not being established in the mus'hafs. In al-Mujtaba: There is no dispute that Ameen is not from the Quran, such that they said that one who says it is from the Quran commits apostasy. And it is sunnah for the one praying alone, imam, follower, and reciter outside prayer. Ameen has four pronunciations; the most eloquent and famous is with elongation and lightening (madd and takhfeedh); because its origin is 'Ya Ameen' meaning 'respond to our supplication', and it is one of Allah's names, but the vocative was dropped, so elongation took its place. The meaning: 'respond'. It is a sound naming the action which is 'istajib' (respond). And from Ibn Abbas: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the meaning of Ameen, and he said: 'Do'. It is said: it is an Arabization of 'Haymana' meaning 'I hope' or 'it should hope'. The poet said (al-Basit): 'O Lord, You are possessor of favor and forgiveness...' and the second (with short alif and lightening) as the poet said (al-Tawil): 'Be distant from me, Fahl, if I call you Ameen, and Allah increased what is between us.'
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on saying Ameen after reciting al-Fatihah in prayer. It is sunnah for all: imam, follower, and individual. The proof is a hadith that promises forgiveness for whose Ameen coincides with the angels' Ameen, interpreted as sincerity, not simultaneity. The passage clarifies that Ameen is not part of the Quran, and declaring it so is apostasy. It discusses its linguistic derivation: originally 'Ya Ameen' (O responder), a name of Allah, shortened with lengthened alif. The meaning is 'respond' or 'do'. It mentions four pronunciations, the most common being with madd (long alif) and takhfeedh (lightening). The poetry lines illustrate usage. The passage also notes that it is sunnah for reciters outside prayer as well.

Key Terms
التأمين (al-ta'min): Saying 'Ameen' after reciting al-Fatihah, meaning 'O Allah, respond'.
آمين (ameen): A word meaning 'respond' or 'do', a name of Allah, used as a supplication.
الملائكة (al-mala'ikah): Angels who say Ameen to the prayers of believers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on saying Ameen in prayer?
A) It is wajib and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is sunnah for the imam only.
C) It is sunnah for the imam, follower, and individual.
D) It is haram to say Ameen aloud.

Key Takeaway
Ameen is a sunnah prayer not from the Quran; saying it with sincerity brings forgiveness.

The Ruling and Pronunciation of Amin in Prayer
Explains the ruling, proof, and linguistic variants of Amin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Amin, identify its proof from the Sunnah, and distinguish the correct pronunciation from incorrect ones, including the effect on the prayer's validity.

Core Idea
Saying Amin is Sunnah, not part of the Quran; the correct pronunciation is with elongation and lightening.

Saying 'Amin' after al-Fatiha is a common practice in prayer, but many do not know its legal status or the correct way to pronounce it. In this passage, the author clarifies that, according to the Hanafi school, Amin is a Sunnah act for everyone in prayer, supported by authentic hadith. He also explains that Amin is not part of the Quran by consensus and discusses the various pronunciations, highlighting which are acceptable and which are errors. Understanding these details ensures that your prayer is performed correctly and in accordance with the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (saying Amin) and the hukm level. The text explicitly states it is Sunnah for the imam, follower, and one praying alone.
The term 'yusann' indicates a recommended act, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary proof cited. The author quotes the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'When the imam says Amin, say Amin...' This is a command (amr) which in Hanafi usul usually indicates obligation, but here it is interpreted as recommendation due to qualifying conditions.
The condition of coincidence with the angels' Amin is not fully within human control, weakening the obligation.
3
Analyze the meaning of 'coincidence'
Understand that the 'coincidence' mentioned in the hadith refers to sincerity and trust in Allah, not simultaneous utterance. This clarifies that the virtue is attained through heartfelt devotion, not mere timing.
4
Confirm the consensus on Amin not being from the Quran
Recognize that all scholars agree Amin is not part of the Quran; denying this consensus leads to apostasy. This established fact prevents confusion and misrecitation.
This is a foundational point that impacts the ruling: it is Sunnah, not an obligatory recitation.
5
Distinguish the linguistic variants and their legal effect
The author lists four pronunciations: (1) madd + takhfif (most preferred), (2) qasr + takhfif, (3) imalah, (4) madd + tashdid. The last two are considered errors. Determine whether these errors invalidate the prayer: the mufta bihi is that they do not, because similar errors occur in Quranic recitation and do not nullify.
Some scholars, like in al-Tajnis, held that tashdid invalidates, but the relied-upon position is that it does not.

ممدوداً ولا يبعد فساد الصلاة فيهما. انتهى. وفيه إشارة إلى أنها مع التشديد لا تفسد بالمد والتخفيف مع حذف الياء لوجوده في القرآن
And Amin. (The term) obligation in their speech means affirmation, end. (And) it is Sunnah (Amin) for the imam, the follower, and the one praying alone, due to his saying: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin, for verily whoever's Amin coincides with the Amin of the angels, his previous sins are forgiven' agreed upon, and in Majma' al-Riwayat it added 'and what came later.' And the meaning of coincidence is sincerity and trust in Allah Almighty, not coincidence in uttering it at one time. Al-Azhari said: 'Ghafara lahu' means he supplicated for him, and 'Ghafara' means he supplicated against him, because al-ghafr is annihilation, end from al-Mustasfa and al-Diraya. And in a narration of al-Bukhari: 'When the imam says 'Ghair al-maghdubi alayhim wa la al-dallin' then say: Amin.' And in Muslim: 'When one of you says in prayer Amin.' Al-Haqq said: In this narration, the one praying alone is included. And in al-Kashshaf, it is narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'Jibril taught me Amin when I finished al-Fatihah and said: It is like a seal on the book.' And it is not from the Quran because it is not established in the mushafs. And in al-Mujtaba: There is no dispute that Amin is not from the Quran, even to the point that they said the one who says it is from the Quran becomes an apostate. And it is Sunnah for the one praying alone, the imam, the follower, and the reciter outside prayer. And Amin has four languages, the most eloquent and famous being with elongation and lightening, because its origin is 'Ya Amin, respond to our supplication,' and it is one of the names of Allah Almighty, except that the vocative was dropped and elongation took its place, and the meaning is 'respond.' And it is a sound that names the action which is 'respond.' And from Ibn Abbas: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the meaning of Amin and he said: 'Do.' And it is said: it is the Arabization of 'Haiman' meaning 'I desire' or 'it should be.' The poet said: [al-Basit]: O Lord, You are the possessor of bounty and forgiveness, establish with well-being the night of the lovers. O Lord, do not deprive me of her love ever, and may Allah have mercy on a servant who said: Amina. And the second is with shortening of the alif and lightening, as the poet said: [al-Tawil]: ‘Tabaa’ada anni Fathal in da’autuhu Amin fa zada Allahu ma baynana.’ (Then continues on the next page) And Tahmid, and silent recitation.. These two are well-known, and on the two languages the word is built on fath, like 'kaifa' and 'ayna', due to the meeting of two saakin letters, and the silence of the noon is permissible in them. The elongation is the choice of the jurists because it agrees with what is narrated from the Prophet, and the shortening is the choice of the literati. The third is with imalah, and the fourth with elongation and tashdid, and the last two were narrated by al-Wahidi. And the meaning of the statement that tashdid is a gross error is that it is nothing. And it is said: its meaning is 'intending the prayer' because of his statement ‘wa la al-dallin.’ And from Shams al-A’imma al-Halwani there is a face for it, because then its meaning is 'We call You intending Your response' out of care for the prayer of the common people. And from Ja’far al-Sadiq and al-Husayn ibn al-Fadl that they recited it like that, and the prayer is not invalidated by it because there is error in the Quran, and the fatwa is upon it. And it is said: it invalidates, as in al-Tajnis. And he said in al-Bahr: And whoever drops the ya’ as a shortened or lengthened form, the corruption of the prayer is not far-fetched in them. End. And in it there is an indication that with tashdid it is not invalid, nor with elongation and lightening with dropping the ya’ because it exists in the Quran.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion probe on the ruling of Amin in prayer. The author states the Hanafi ruling that saying Amin is Sunnah for imam, follower, and one praying alone. The textual proof is the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin...' The author clarifies that 'coincidence' with the angels' Amin means sincerity and trust, not simultaneous utterance. He also mentions that Amin is not part of the Quran by consensus, and denying that is apostasy. Then he discusses the four pronunciations of Amin: (1) madd (elongation) and takhfif (lightening) — the most famous and preferred by jurists; (2) qasr (shortening) and takhfif — preferred by literary scholars; (3) imalah; (4) madd with tashdid (doubling). The latter two are rare and considered errors. The author quotes poetry to illustrate the pronunciations. He also addresses the issue of whether saying Amin with tashdid invalidates the prayer. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it does not invalidate because similar errors occur in Quranic recitation. The passage concludes with a subtle indication that only the pronunciation with tashdid is acceptable, but elongation and lightening with dropping the ya' (silent letter) is also valid as it exists in the Quran.

Key Terms
تأمين (ta'min): The act of saying Amin in prayer.
آمين (Amin): A word meaning 'respond, O Allah' or 'accept', not part of the Quran.
لغات (lughat): The different modes of pronunciation of Amin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Saying Amin is a Sunnah act in prayer, not part of the Quran, and the correct pronunciation is with a long alif and lightened m, though other variants are acceptable and do not invalidate the prayer.
