والصَّلاة على سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الجلوس الأخير، (و) من الصَّلاةُ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا النَّبِيِّ في الجلوس الأخير؛ لقوله : ( إِذَا تَشَهدَ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي الصَّلاةِ فَلْيَقُلْ: اللهمَّ صَلَّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ وَبَارِكْ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، وَارْحَمْ مُحَمَّدَاً وآلِ مُحَمَّدٍ كَمَا صَلَّيْتَ وَبَارَكْتَ وَتَرَحَمْتَ عَلَى إبْرَاهِيمَ، وَعَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ ). رواه البيهقي والحاكم. وسئل محمد رحمه الله عن كيفية الصلاة على النبي ، فقال: يقول اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد، كما صليت على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم، وبارك على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما باركت على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم إنك حميد مجيد، كذا في « التبيين» من غير ذكر في العالمين، وهي ثابتة في رواية أبي مسعود الأنصاري عند مالك ومسلم وأبي داود وغيرهم. وفي ( إفصاح ) ابن هبيرة عن محمد بن الحسن ذكر الصلاة المنقولة عنه مع زيادة « في العالمين»، فما في «السراج» وغيره من أنه لا يأتي بها ضعيف، ومعنى الصلاة: الرحمة، وإنما كرر حرف الجر في الآل للإشارة إلى تراخي رتبة آله عنه، واختلف فيهم، والأكثرون على أنهم قرابته الذين حرمت عليهم الصدقة، وصححه بعضهم، واختار النووي أنهم جميع الأمة، وروي عن بعض المشايخ أنه لا يقول : وارحم محمداً، وأكثر المشايخ على أنه يقوله للتوارث، وقال السرخسي: لا بأس به لأن الأثر ورد به من طريق أبي هريرة، وابن عباس ، وإن أحداً و إن جل قدره لا يستغني عن رحمة الله. قال وصححه عامة المشايخ، ومحل الخلاف في الجواز وعدمـه إنمـا هـو فـيمـا
And (it is sunnah to send) salawat upon our master the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the final sitting; because of his saying: 'When one of you recites tashahhud in prayer, let him say: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, and bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, and have mercy upon Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You sent blessings, blessings, and mercy upon Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim; indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious.' Narrated by al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) was asked about the manner of sending salawat upon the Prophet, so he said: He says: 'O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and the family of Muhammad as You sent blessings upon Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim, and bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad as You blessed Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim; indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious.' Thus in al-Tabyin without mentioning 'in the worlds'. And it is established in the narration of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari according to Malik, Muslim, Abu Dawud and others. And in Ifsah of Ibn Hubayrah from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, the transmitted salawat includes the addition 'in the worlds'. So what is in al-Siraj and others that he does not come with it is weak. The meaning of salat is mercy. And he repeated the preposition in 'al' to indicate the lower rank of his family compared to him. They differed about who they are; the majority say they are his relatives for whom sadaqah is forbidden, and some authenticated that. Al-Nawawi chose that they are the entire ummah. And it is narrated from some mashayikh that he does not say 'wa arham Muhammad', but the majority of mashayikh say he says it because of inheritance. Al-Sarakhsi said: There is no problem with it because the report came from Abu Hurairah and Ibn Abbas, and no one, however great his rank, is independent of Allah's mercy. He said, and the majority of mashayikh authenticated it. The place of dispute in permissibility or impermissibility is only in...
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of sending salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet Muhammad in the final sitting of prayer after tashahhud. The authority is a hadith indicating the wording. The text presents the version without 'fi al-alamin' as the one reported by Muhammad al-Shaybani, while another version includes it. The majority of Hanafi scholars accept the wording including 'wa arham' (have mercy). Al-Sarakhsi justifies it as no one is free from need of mercy. The passage also discusses the meaning of 'al' (family) and the differing opinions on who they are.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad.
الآل (al-al): The family of the Prophet, specifically those for whom sadaqah is forbidden according to the majority of Hanafis.

A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Fard
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Sending salawat upon the Prophet in the final tashahhud is a sunnah, and the preferred wording includes 'wa arham' and 'fi al-alamin' according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Obligation of Salawat Once in a Lifetime; Sunnah in Prayer
Explains obligation of salawat and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending salawat upon the Prophet and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi, including the ruling within prayer.

Core Idea
Sending blessings on the Prophet is fard once in a lifetime; in prayer it is sunnah, not wajib.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah clarifies the Hanafi position on the obligation of sending salawat upon the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ. It addresses a common misconception that salawat must be recited in every prayer, and details the differences between two great Hanafi imams: al-Karkhi, who holds it necessary once in a lifetime, and al-Tahawi, who holds it obligatory every time the Prophet is mentioned. Through understanding this dispute, you will see how the school's relied-upon view is derived from Qur'anic commands and hadith, and why salawat in tashahhud remains sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the tanbih: 'al-salat 'ala al-nabi fard 'indana fi al-umr marra.' This is the central ruling: sending blessings once in a lifetime is fard. Note the key term 'fard' and that it is limited to once in a lifetime.
Fard here means obligatory by decisive evidence (qat'i).
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Find where al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi differ. Al-Karkhi says the command (amm) does not imply repetition, so fard once. Al-Tahawi says obligation repeats when the cause (dhikr) repeats, making it wajib upon each mention.
The dispute is about obligation upon mention, not in prayer.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence for sunnah in prayer
The passage cites a hadith giving choice ('if you wish to stand, stand'), which negates wujub. This is the key evidence that salawat in prayer is sunnah, not wajib.
The hadith is used by Hanafis to override any apparent command.
4
Refute opposing hadith
The text refutes the hadith 'La salata' by declaring it weak (da'if) and offers alternative interpretations if accepted. This shows critical hadith evaluation.
Even if authentic, 'complete' or 'in his lifetime' are possible meanings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of al-Karkhi: fard once in a lifetime. However, many later Hanafis follow al-Tahawi's precautionary view of wajib upon mention.
In prayer, all Hanafis agree it is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقال: مضموماً إلى الصلاة والسلام، كما أفاده شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر ، فلذا اتفقوا على أنه لا يقول ابتداء رحمه الله، وفي « الدراية » فإن قيل: كيف قال: « كما صليت على إبراهيم إلخ، والمشبه دون المشبه به، وهو أكرم على الله من إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام. قلنا: ذاك قبل أن يُبَيِّن الله له منزلته عليه الصلاة والسلام، فلما بين أبقى الدعوة، أو تشبيهه لأصل الصلاة بأصل الصلاة لا القدر، كما في قوله تعالى: كيب عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ كَمَا كُتِبَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٣]، أو التشبيه وقع في الصلاة على الآل لا عليه، فكان قوله : ( اللهم صل على محمد » ، منقطعاً عن التشبيه، أو المشبه الصلاة على محمد وآله، بالصلاة على إبراهيم وآله ومعظم الأنبياء، آل إبراهيم فإذا تقابلت الجملة بالجملة يقدر أن يكون آل رسول كآل إبراهيم، والحميد بمعنى المحمود، أي: مستحق لجميع أنواع المحامد، عدل إلى صيغة المبالغة، والمجيد بمعنى الماجد وهو من كمل في الشرف والكرم والصفات المحمودة. انتهى. والنكتة في تخصيص سيدنا إبراهيم دون غيره من الأنبياء: إما سلامه على أمة محمد ليلة الإسراء دون غيره من الأنبياء، أو لدعائه بقوله: ﴿رَبَّنَا وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْهُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٢٩]، أو لأنه سمانا المسلمين، وسماه الله أبا المسلمين، وحسن الختم بأنك حميد مجيد، لأن الداعي يشرع له أن يختم دعاءه باسم من الأسماء الحسنى مناسب لمطلوبه، ولقصورنا عن القيام بحق الصلاة المأمور بها في الآية الشريفة، سألناها من الله، ونسبتها إلينا مجاز، لأن المصلي حقيقة هو الله على نبيه .
(۲)
تنبيه: الصلاة على النبي فرض عندنا في العمر مرة، كما قال الكرخي: إذ لا يقتضي الأمر التكرار، وقال الطحاوي تفترض كلما ذكر لا لأن الأمر يقتضي التكرار، بل لأنه تعلق وجوبها بسبب مكرر، وهو الذكر، فتكرر بتكرره، فأما كونها واجبة في الصلاة للصلاة، فلا دلالة عليه انتهى؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا وَفَعَلْتَ هَدَاء " إلخ، وقوله : ( إن شئت أن تقم فقم (۳)، والتخيير ينافي الفرضية والوجوب، فيقول المباح فتكون الصلاة عليه صلى الله عليه وسلم في الصلاة سنة كما في « الدراية»، وما روي عنه لا صلاةَ لِمَنْ لم يصل علي » ) ضعفه أهل الحديث كلهم، وعلى فرض صحته فمعناه كاملة، أو لمن لم يصل علي في عمره، وكذا ما جاء في حديث ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( مَنْ صَلَّى صَلاةٌ لَمْ يُصَلِّ عَلَيَّ فِيهَا وَعَلَى آلِ بَيْتِي لَمْ تُقْبَلَ مِنْه" (۱) ضعيف بجابر الجعفي مع أنه قد اختلف في رفعه ووقفه كذا في « البرهان».
فائدة: لا يجب على النبي أن يصلي على نفسه، كذا في «معراج الدراية».
It is said: included with the prayers and salutations, as stated by Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar. Therefore they agreed that one should not begin with 'rahimahullah'. And in al-Dirayah: If it is said: How did he say 'as You sent blessings upon Ibrahim etc.' while the compared is inferior to the compared-to, and he [Muhammad] is more honored by Allah than Ibrahim (peace be upon him)? We reply: That was before Allah showed him his station (peace be upon him). When it was shown, he retained the supplication. Or the comparison is of the essence of the prayer with the essence of the prayer, not the measure, as in His statement: 'Fasting is prescribed for you as it was prescribed for those before you' [al-Baqarah 183]. Or the comparison occurs in the prayer upon the family, not upon him, so his statement 'O Allah, bless Muhammad' is separate from the comparison. Or the compared is the prayer upon Muhammad and his family with the prayer upon Ibrahim and his family, and most prophets are the family of Ibrahim. Thus, when the sentences correspond, it is estimated that the family of the Messenger is like the family of Ibrahim. And al-Hamid means the Praised One, i.e., deserving all types of praise; the intensive form is used. And al-Majid means the Glorious, i.e., the one perfect in honor, generosity, and praiseworthy attributes. End. And the subtlety in specifying our master Ibrahim over other prophets: either because he greeted the ummah of Muhammad on the night of Isra without other prophets, or because of his supplication: 'Our Lord, send among them a messenger from themselves' [al-Baqarah 129], or because he named us Muslims and Allah named him the father of Muslims. And the conclusion with 'Indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious' is good because the supplicant should conclude his supplication with an appropriate name from the beautiful names. Due to our incapacity to fulfill the right of the commanded prayer in the noble verse, we ask it from Allah; its attribution to us is metaphorical, because the real sender of blessings is Allah upon His Prophet. (2) Note: Sending blessings upon the Prophet is obligatory in our school once in a lifetime, as al-Karkhi said: because the command does not entail repetition. Al-Tahawi said: It becomes obligatory every time he is mentioned, not because the command entails repetition, but because its obligation is tied to a repeated cause (remembrance), so it repeats with its repetition. As for it being obligatory in prayer, there is no indication for that, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'When you say this and do this...' and his statement: 'If you wish to stand, stand.' Choice negates obligation and necessity, so it is said to be permissible, thus sending blessings upon him (peace be upon him) in prayer is sunnah, as in al-Dirayah. And what is narrated: 'No prayer for the one who does not send blessings upon me' has been declared weak by all hadith scholars. Even if authentic, it means 'complete' or 'for the one who does not send blessings upon me in his lifetime'. Likewise, the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever prays a prayer in which he does not send blessings upon me and upon my family, it is not accepted from him' is weak due to Jabir al-Ju'fi, and there is disagreement on its being marfu' and mauquf. This is in al-Burhan. Benefit: The Prophet is not required to send blessings upon himself, as in Miraj al-Dirayah.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of sending salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ. It begins with a subtle discussion from al-Dirayah explaining why the comparison to Ibrahim (AS) in the tasbih is valid, despite the Prophet being superior. The core point is that the comparison is in the essence of the prayer, not the degree. The passage then provides a 'tanbih' (note) that outlines the intra-Hanafi dispute on the obligation of salawat. Imam al-Karkhi holds that it is obligatory once in a lifetime because the command (from Qur'an 33:56) does not indicate repetition. Imam al-Tahawi holds that it becomes obligatory every time the Prophet ﷺ is mentioned, because the cause (dhikr) repeats. However, both agree that it is not obligated specifically within the prayer (i.e., during tashahhud). The text cites a hadith giving a choice, which negates wujub; thus, in the Hanafi school, salawat in prayer is sunnah, not wajib. The text then refutes hadiths that seem to suggest otherwise, declaring them weak or reinterpreted. Finally, a 'fa'ida' notes that the Prophet himself is not required to send blessings upon himself. The Hanafi position here is that salawat is fard (obligatory) once in a lifetime, and in prayer it is sunnah. This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf with the relied-upon (mufta bihi) being the view of al-Karkhi and the majority that it is fard once in a lifetime, though many later Hanafis follow al-Tahawi's view of obligation upon mention (wajib). The authority weight is from the foundational texts of the school (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): The act of sending blessings and peace upon the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, as commanded in Qur'an 33:56.
فرض (fard): An obligation that must be performed; omission without excuse is sinful. In this context, sending salawat once in a lifetime is fard.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed; leaving it is not sinful but disliked. Here, salawat in prayer is sunnah, not wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sending salawat upon the Prophet in prayer?
A) It is wajib in every tashahhud.
B) It is fard once in a lifetime and sunnah in prayer.
C) It is haram to omit it.
D) It is only recommended outside of prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sending salawat upon the Prophet is fard once in a lifetime; in prayer it is sunnah, not wajib, as per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Du'a in Prayer: Ruling and Permissible Wording
States ruling and provides expansion with examples and a prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making du'a after salawat in prayer and identify which words are permissible according to the text.

Core Idea
Du'a after salawat is sunnah, using words resembling Quran and Sunnah, but not imitating them exactly.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the recommended supplication after the tashahhud and salawat. The author cites a hadith and provides examples from the Prophet and companions, while clarifying a crucial prohibition: du'a should not be made with words that exactly mimic Quranic phrasing or prophetic traditions in a way that could be mistaken for recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making du'a (supplication) after sending blessings upon the Prophet in prayer. The ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
The phrase 'yusannu al-du'a' indicates sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of the Prophet: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with praising Allah... then send blessings upon the Prophet, then make du'a as he wishes.' Tirmidhi declared it sahih.
This establishes the recommendation and the order.
3
Understand the expansion on wording
The author specifies that the du'a should be with words that 'resemble' (yushbihu) the wording of the Quran and Sunnah. Examples include Quranic verses like 'Rabbana la tuzigh qulubana' and various prophetic supplications.
The examples show that using actual Quranic verses or prophetic du'as is permissible when intended as supplication.
4
Analyze the prohibition
The text ends with 'la' (no), stating it is not permissible to make du'a with words that resemble the wording of the Quran and Sunnah. This forbids using exact wording in a manner that imitates revelation, i.e., recitation with the intention of tilawah.
The prohibition is against confusion between recitation and supplication, not against using the words themselves.
5
Apply to examples
The examples given (Abu Bakr's du'a, Ibn Mas'ud's, Aishah's, Ibn Abbas's) are all from the Sunnah, showing that these specific supplications are recommended. The prohibition applies to invented phrases that mimic Quranic style or using Quranic verses with the intent of recitation.
Distinguish between du'a (supplication) and tilawah (recitation).

(و) يسن ( الدُّعَاءُ) بعد الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لقوله : ( إِذَا صَلَّى أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَبْدَا بِتَحْمِيدِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، وَالثَّنَاءِ عَلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ لَيُصَلِّ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ، ثُمَّ لْيَدْعُو بَعْدُ مَا شَاءَ » (۳)، قال الترمذي: حديث صحيح، لكن في الصلاة يدعو ( بِمَا يُشبِهُ الْفَاظَ القرآنِ)، كقوله: ﴿رَبَّنَا لَا تُزِغْ قُلُوبَنَا [ آل عمران: ۸] الآية (وَالسُّنَّةِ) بالنصب، عطفاً على ألفاظ القرآن والجر، عطفاً على بما، ومن السنة ما روي عن أبي بكره أنه قال لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : علمني يا رسول الله دعاء أدعو به في صَلاتِي، فقال: « قُل، اللهم إني ظلمت نفسي ظلماً كثيراً، وإنَّهُ لا يغفر الذنوب إلا أنت فاغفر لي مغفرةً من عندك وارحمني إنك أنت الغفور الرحيم» (۳)، وكان ابن مسعود له يدعو بكلمات منهن : « اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أسْأَلُكَ مِنْ الْخَيْرِ كُلِّهِ مَا عَلِمْتُ مِنْهُ، وَمَا لَمْ أعْلَمْ، وَأعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ الشَّرِّ كُلِّهِ مَا عَلِمْتُ مِنْهُ، وَمَا لَمْ أَعْلَمْ ) وعن عائشة : كَانَ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَدْعُو فِي الصَّلاةِ: اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ عَذَابِ الْقَبْرِ ، وَمِنْ فِتْنَةِ الْمَسِيحِ الدَّجَّالِ، وَأَعوذُ بِكَ مِنْ فِتْنَةِ الْمَحْيَا وَفِتْنَةِ الْمَمَاتِ، اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ الْمَأْثَمِ وَالْمَغْرَمِ ) ()، وعن ابن عباس له أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يعلمهم هذا الدعاء، كما يعلمهم السورة من القرآن: «اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ عَذَابِ جَهَنَّمَ، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ عَذَابِ الْقَبْرِ، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ فِتْنَةِ الْمَسِيحِ الدَّجَّالِ، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ فِتْنَةِ الْمَحْيَا وَالْمَمَاتِ » كذا في ( الدراية»، (لا)، أي لا يجوز أن يدعو في صلاته، بمـا يشبه ألفاظ القرآن والسنّة، لا.
(And) it is sunnah to make du'a after sending blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, because of his statement: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with praising Allah and extolling Him, then send blessings upon the Prophet, then let him make du'a after that as he wishes.' (Tirmidhi said: This is a sound hadith). However, in prayer, one should make du'a with words resembling the wording of the Qur'an, such as his statement: 'Our Lord, do not make our hearts deviate...' (Al Imran: 8) and the Sunnah (with accusative case as a conjunction on 'words of the Qur'an' or genitive as a conjunction on 'what' [i.e., with words resembling the wording of the Qur'an and the Sunnah]). From the Sunnah is what is narrated from Abu Bakr, that he said to the Messenger of Allah: Teach me, O Messenger of Allah, a du'a that I can make in my prayer. He said: 'Say: O Allah, I have greatly wronged myself, and none forgives sins except You, so forgive me with a forgiveness from You and have mercy on me, indeed You are the Oft-Forgiving, the Most Merciful.' (Bukhari, Muslim). And Ibn Mas'ud used to make du'a with words including: 'O Allah, I ask You for all good, what I know and what I do not know, and I seek refuge in You from all evil, what I know and what I do not know.' (narrated by Ibn Majah). And from Aishah: The Prophet ﷺ used to make du'a in prayer: 'O Allah, I seek refuge in You from the torment of the grave, and from the trial of the False Messiah, and I seek refuge in You from the trial of life and death. O Allah, I seek refuge in You from sin and debt.' (Bukhari, Muslim). And from Ibn Abbas: He ﷺ used to teach them this du'a just as he taught them a surah of the Qur'an: 'O Allah, I seek refuge in You from the torment of Hell, and I seek refuge in You from the torment of the grave, and I seek refuge in You from the trial of the False Messiah, and I seek refuge in You from the trial of life and death.' This is in al-Dirayah. (No), i.e., it is not permissible to make du'a in prayer with words that resemble the wording of the Qur'an and the Sunnah. No.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of making du'a (supplication) in prayer. It begins by stating that it is sunnah to make du'a after sending blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, based on a hadith from Tirmidhi. The text then clarifies that the du'a should be with words that resemble the Qur'an and Sunnah — meaning, the du'a should be similar to the phrasing found in the Quran or the prophetic traditions. Examples are given: the Quranic verse 'Rabbana la tuzigh qulubana' and supplications taught by the Prophet to Abu Bakr, Ibn Mas'ud, Aishah, and Ibn Abbas. However, the last part ('la') introduces a prohibition: it is not permissible to make du'a with words that exactly imitate or resemble the Quran and Sunnah in a way that creates confusion or implies that one is reciting them as part of the prayer text. In other words, one should not use the exact wording of the Quran in du'a outside of recitation, nor use words that are uniquely Quranic or prophetic in a manner that mimics revelation. The Hanafi position is that du'a in prayer is sunnah, but it must be with permissible words — not with the exact wording of the Quran (which would be considered recitation) and not with innovations. The examples given are all from the Sunnah, so they are recommended. The prohibition is against inventing or using phrases that are specific to the Quran or Sunnah in a way that could be mistaken for obligatory recitation. This teaching preserves the distinction between the recited Qur'an and personal supplication.

Key Terms
الدعاء (al-du'a): Supplication to Allah; in this context, the personal request made after the tashahhud and salawat in prayer.
بما يشبه ألفاظ القرآن والسنّة (bima yushbihu alfaz al-quran wa al-sunnah): Words that resemble the phrasing of the Quran and the prophetic traditions; allowed in du'a, but not identical wording that would imply recitation.
سنن (sunan): Plural of sunnah; recommended acts. Here it refers to the prophetic supplications that are recommended for du'a in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true about du'a in prayer according to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage?
A) Du'a is wajib after salawat.
B) Du'a is not allowed; it should only be praise.
C) Du'a is sunnah, but must not use words that exactly imitate the Quran or Sunnah in a confusing manner.
D) Du'a can be in any language.

Key Takeaway
Making du'a after salawat is a confirmed sunnah, and the worshipper should use words from the Quran (as supplication) or the prophetic traditions, avoiding exact imitation that could confuse the prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Permissible and Prohibited Du'a in Prayer: The Hanafi View
Ruling on du'a in prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and prohibited forms of du'a in prayer according to the Hanafi school and apply the hadith 'لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس' to identify which du'as are allowed.

Core Idea
In prayer, du'a must resemble Quran and Sunnah; anything that could be asked of a human is prohibited.

When we pray, we often make supplications. But are all forms of du'a acceptable during prayer? The Hanafi school, relying on a key hadith, distinguishes between du'a that is in the style of divine speech and du'a that resembles ordinary human requests. This lesson will guide you through the evidence, the ruling, and the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is du'a during prayer. The Hanafi ruling: du'a resembling kalam al-nas is prohibited (haram); du'a resembling Quran and Sunnah is permissible.
The passage explicitly says 'لا يجوز' for kalam al-nas.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'إن صلاتنا هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس' (This prayer of ours is not suitable for anything from the speech of people).
This is a hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawood.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا يصلح' indicates negation of suitability, which implies prohibition. 'شيء من كلام الناس' generalizes all human speech, including du'a that resembles it. Thus, any du'a that could be asked of a human is prohibited.
The Hanafis interpret 'لا يصلح' as a prohibition (tahrim).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i allows any du'a in prayer, citing the hadith: 'ثم يتخير أحدكم من الدعاء أعجبه إليه فيدعو به' (Then let each of you choose the supplication most pleasing to him).
The Hanafi response: the prohibiting hadith (man'ah) takes precedence over the permitting one (mubih).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis restrict in-prayer du'a to Quranic and prophetic forms, while Shafi'is allow any du'a, including requests for worldly matters.
This difference affects everyday practice.

(۲) أخرجه الترمذي في الدعوات، باب: (٦٥) (٣٤٧٧)، والحاكم في المستدرك (٢٣٠/١). (۳) أخرجه البخاري في الأذان، باب الدعاء قبل السلام (٨٣٤) ، ومسلم في الدعوات، باب: ا الصوت بالذكر (٢٧٠٥). (٥) أخرجه البخاري في الأذان، باب الدعاء قبل السلام (۸۳۲)، ومسلم في المساجد ومواضع الصلاة، باب: مـا يستعاذ في الصلاة (٥٨٩). (٦) أخرجه مسلم في المساجد ومواضع الصلاة، باب ما يستعاذ منه في الصلاة (٥٩٠)، وابن ماجه في الدعاء، باب ما تعوذ منه الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ( ٣٨٤٠ ). كلام الناس، والالتفات يميناً، ثمّ يساراً، بالتسليمتين. ونيّةُ الإمام الرِّجالَ، والحَفَظَةَ . And supplication that resembles the words of the Quran and Sunnah is [permissible]; no. [Hadith] from Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays a prayer and does not send blessings upon me and upon my family, it is not accepted from him.' Weak due to Jabir al-Ju'fi, and there is disagreement on whether it is marfu' or mawquf, as in al-Burhan. Benefit: It is not obligatory for the Prophet to send blessings upon himself, as in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. (And) it is sunnah (supplication) after sending blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, because of his saying: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with praise of Allah Almighty and glorification, then send blessings upon the Prophet, then supplicate afterwards whatever he wishes.' Al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih. But in prayer, he supplicates (with what resembles the words of the Quran), such as: 'Our Lord, do not let our hearts deviate...' (Surah Al-Imran: 8), and (the Sunnah) – with nasb as a conjunction on 'words of the Quran' and with jarr as a conjunction on 'with what'. From the Sunnah is what is narrated from Abu Bakr that he said to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Teach me, O Messenger of Allah, a supplication that I may make in my prayer.' He said: 'Say: O Allah, I have wronged myself greatly, and no one forgives sins except You, so grant me forgiveness from Yourself and have mercy on me; indeed, You are the Oft-Forgiving, the Most Merciful.' Ibn Mas'ud used to supplicate with words including: 'O Allah, I ask You for all good, what I know of it and what I do not know, and I seek refuge with You from all evil, what I know of it and what I do not know.' And from A'ishah: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to supplicate in prayer: 'O Allah, I seek refuge with You from the punishment of the grave, and from the trial of the False Messiah, and I seek refuge with You from the trial of life and the trial of death. O Allah, I seek refuge with You from sin and debt.' And from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to teach them this supplication as he taught them a surah of the Quran: 'O Allah, I seek refuge with You from the punishment of Hellfire, and I seek refuge with You from the punishment of the grave, and I seek refuge with You from the trial of the False Messiah, and I seek refuge with You from the trial of life and death.' As in al-Dirayah. (No), meaning it is not permissible for him to supplicate in his prayer with what resembles the speech of people, because of his saying: 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for anything from the speech of people.' Whatever is not impossible to ask from them is from their speech. And this is given precedence over the hadith: 'Then let each of you choose the supplication that is most pleasing to him and supplicate with it,' because it is a prohibition and this is a permission. Our companions interpreted 'what resembles the speech of people' as that which is not impossible to ask from other than Allah Almighty, such as saying: 'Give me such-and-such a position,' 'Marry me to so-and-so,' 'Provide me with a beautiful slave-girl,' while what is impossible [to ask from them] like forgiveness, well-being, and pardon. As in al-Dirayah, from al-Idah.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on supplication (du'a) in prayer, with proofs from hadith. The author first addresses the issue of sending blessings (salawat) on the Prophet in prayer: a weak hadith suggests it is required, but the stronger view is that it is not obligatory for the Prophet to send blessings on himself. It is sunnah to send blessings and then to supplicate after the prayer. During prayer, the supplication should resemble the words of the Quran and the Sunnah; the text gives examples of permissible du'as from the Quran (e.g., 'Rabbana la tuzigh qulubana'), from the Sunnah (e.g., the du'a taught to Abu Bakr, the du'as of Ibn Mas'ud, A'ishah, and Ibn 'Abbas). The key ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz) to supplicate with words that resemble the speech of people (kalam al-nas). The proof is the hadith: 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for anything from the speech of people.' The author explains that 'speech of people' means anything that could reasonably be requested from another human being, such as asking for a job or marriage. In contrast, du'as that ask for what can only come from Allah—like forgiveness and well-being—are permissible. This prohibition overrides a hadith that allows any du'a, because a prohibiting text takes precedence over a permitting one. The Hanafi position thus restricts in-prayer du'a to forms that are Quranic or prophetic in style, avoiding mundane requests.

Key Terms
كلام الناس (kalam al-nas): Speech that is characteristic of human conversation, including requests that could be made to another person.
ما يستحيل سؤاله من غير الله (ma yastahilu su'aluhu min ghayr Allah): What cannot be asked from anyone other than Allah, such as forgiveness, well-being, and paradise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following du'as is NOT permissible in prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) 'Rabbi inni zalamtu nafsi'
B) 'Allahumma inni as'aluka al-afiyah'
C) 'Allahumma zawwijni fulanah'
D) 'Allahumma inni a'udhu bika min 'adhabi jahannam'

Key Takeaway
Du'a in prayer must be in the style of Quran and Sunnah; requests that could be made to humans are prohibited.

Sunnah of Taslim: Turning, Wording, and Rulings on Mistakes
Ruling with proof and practical applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions of taslim (turning and wording), cite the hadith proof, and apply the rulings on mistakes in taslim.

Core Idea
Turning right then left with two taslims is sunnah, supported by the Prophet's practice; errors require corrective action.

This lesson covers the sunnah of concluding prayer with taslim—the turning of the face, the wording, and what to do if mistakes occur. The Hanafi school emphasizes that both the turning and the specific phrasing are sunnah, not obligatory, but following them brings completeness to the prayer. The hadith from al-Tirmidhi provides the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main sunnah action
The act of turning to the right then to the left with two taslims is described as sunnah. The wording used is 'As-salamu 'alaykum wa rahmatullah'.
The turning should be enough for the cheek to be visible from behind.
2
Examine the hadith proof (dalil)
The hadith narrated by the authors of Sunan and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi describes the Prophet's practice of turning right and left until the whiteness of his cheek was visible. This is the evidence for the sunnah.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Understand the sunnah wording and alternatives
The full sunnah is 'As-salamu 'alaykum wa rahmatullah'. Shorter forms like 'As-salamu 'alaykum' suffice but omit the sunnah. Saying ''Alaykum as-salam' is makruh (disliked). Adding 'wa barakatuh' is considered bid'ah by al-Nawawi.
The passage states that ''Alaykum as-salam' is makruh according to al-Siraj.
4
Apply rulings on beginning with the left
If one begins with the left side intentionally or forgetfully, he should still give salam to the right and does not need to repeat the left salam.
The order of turning is not obligatory; the right salam is still valid.
5
Handle forgetfulness of the left salam
If one remembers after standing up that he forgot the left salam, he should return, sit, and perform it as long as he has not spoken or left the mosque. If he has spoken or left, the left salam is no longer required.
This applies only if the omission is remembered in time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن (الالتفات يميناً، ثـم يـسـاراً، بالتسليمتين) لأنه ( كَانَ يُسَلِّمُ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ فَيَقُولُ: السَّلامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ، حَتَّى يُرَى بَيَاضُ حَدِّهِ الْأَيْمَنِ وَعَنْ يَسَارِهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ حَتَّى يُرَى بَيَاضُ خَدِّهِ الأَيْسَرِ » (۳) رواه أصحاب السنن وصححه الترمذي، والسنة أن يخفض صوته في الثانية عن الأولى والأكمل قد علمته من لفظه الشريف فإن قال: السلام عليكم أو السلام، أو سلام عليكم، أو عليكم السلام أجزأه، وكان تاركاً للسنة، وصرح به في «السراج» بكراهة الأخير، وأنه لا يقول وبركاته، وصرح النووي بأنه بدعة)، وليس فيه [ شيء ] ثابت، فلو بدأ بيساره عامداً، أو ناسياً يسلم عن يمينه، ولا يعيده عـلـى يـســاره، ولا شيء عليه، ولو سلم تلقاء وجهه، فإنه يسلم عن يساره، ولو نسي يساره حتى قام يرجع ويقعد ويسلم ما لم يتكلم، أو يخرج من المسجد ).
(And) it is sunnah (to turn one's face) to the right, then to the left, with two taslims, because he (peace be upon him) used to say salam to his right saying 'As-salamu 'alaykum wa rahmatullah' until the whiteness of his right cheek could be seen, and to his left saying 'As-salamu 'alaykum wa rahmatullah' until the whiteness of his left cheek could be seen. Narrated by the authors of the Sunan and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. It is sunnah to lower his voice in the second [taslim] compared to the first, and the most complete [form] you have learned from his noble wording. If he says 'as-salamu 'alaykum' or 'as-salam' or 'salamun 'alaykum' or ''alaykum as-salam', it suffices him, but he is leaving the sunnah. It is stated in al-Siraj that the last [''alaykum as-salam'] is disliked (makruh), and that he should not say 'wa barakatuh'. Al-Nawawi explicitly said it is an innovation (bid'ah), and there is nothing authentic in it. So if he begins with his left intentionally or forgetfully, he gives salam to his right, and does not repeat it to his left, and nothing is upon him. If he gives salam straight ahead, then he gives salam to his left. If he forgets his left until he stands up, he returns, sits, and gives salam as long as he has not spoken or left the mosque.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah actions of the taslim (saying salam) at the end of prayer. The author states that it is sunnah to turn the face to the right when saying the first salam and to the left when saying the second. The proof is the hadith describing the Prophet's practice (peace be upon him): he would turn so much that the whiteness of his cheek became visible. It is also sunnah to lower the voice slightly in the second salam. The minimum acceptable phrasing is 'As-salamu 'alaykum' or similar, but the full sunnah is to say 'As-salamu 'alaykum wa rahmatullah'. Using ''Alaykum as-salam' (starting with 'alaykum') is considered makruh (disliked) and contrary to the sunnah. Adding 'wa barakatuh' is considered a bid'ah (innovation) by many scholars, including al-Nawawi, though some later fatwas differ. If someone mistakenly begins with the left side, they should still say salam to the right and do not need to repeat the left. If they forget the left salam until after standing, they may return and perform it as long as they have not spoken or left the mosque. This provides practical guidelines for the taslim.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): The act of saying salam to end the prayer, consisting of two salam: to the right and to the left.
الالتفات (al-iltifat): Turning the face to the right or left during taslim, to the extent that the cheek becomes visible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must repeat both taslims starting from the right.
B) He gives salam to his right and does not repeat the left.
C) His prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
D) He must return to the right and start over.

Key Takeaway
The practice of taslim in the Hanafi school is sunnah, not obligatory, and includes specific sunnah actions and remedies for common mistakes.

The Imam's Sunnah Intention: Including All Congregants and Angels
Explanation of the sunnah of imam's intention in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions of the imam's intention and explain why the imam should not specify a number for angels.

Core Idea
The imam's intention to include all followers and angels is sunnah; the number of angels is unknown so no number is specified.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the imam's niyyah in congregational prayer. The imam is recommended to intend the men, women, children, and the guardian angels who join the prayer. The text emphasizes that the imam should not attempt to count the angels because the hadith reports vary on their number. Understanding this illustrates how Hanafi fiqh deals with matters beyond human certainty—leaving details general when specifics are not established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's specific intention (niyyah) for the congregation. According to the Hanafi school, this is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
Sunnah here means recommended, not obligatory.
2
List those included in the intention
The text explicitly includes men, women, khuntha (hermaphrodites), children, and al-hafazah (guardian angels). Understand that 'al-hafazah' are angels who record deeds and protect humans.
Khuntha refers to persons of ambiguous gender, ensuring inclusivity.
3
Recognize why no fixed number for angels
Because the hadith reports about the number of angels differ, it is not possible to ascertain a precise count. Therefore, the imam should not specify a number; he should intend them generally.
This resembles belief in the prophets—we believe in them without needing to know exact numbers.
4
Note the source of authority
The passage states 'kadha fi al-Hidayah' (as in al-Hidayah), indicating this ruling is from the authoritative Hanafi text.
Al-Hidayah is a central work of Hanafi fiqh by al-Marghinani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن (نيّة الإمام الرِّجال) ومن معه من النساء والخنائي والصبيان ( والحفظة). جمع حافظ، ككتبة جمع كاتب، وسموا به لحفظهم ما يصدر من الإنسان من قول وعمل، أو لحفظهم إياه من الجن وأسباب المعاطب ) ، ولا ينوي عدداً محصوراً، لأن الأخبار في عددهم قد اختلفت فأشبه الإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام كذا في « الهداية ».
(And) it is sunnah (for the imam to intend) the men, and those with him of women, khuntha (hermaphrodites), and children, and the hafazah (guardian angels). The plural of hafiz, like kuttab (scribes) is plural of katib. They are called so because they preserve what emanates from a person of speech and action, or because they preserve him from jinn and causes of destruction. And he should not intend a fixed number, because the reports about their number have differed, so it resembles belief in the prophets (peace be upon them). As in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of the imam's intention (niyyah) when leading prayer. It is sunnah for the imam to intend to lead the men, women, khuntha (those with ambiguous gender), and children who are praying behind him, as well as the hafazah (guardian angels) who also pray with the congregation. The hafazah are angels who record deeds and protect humans. The author advises that the imam should not intend a specific number of angels because the various hadith reports about their number differ; it is sufficient to believe in their existence in general, similar to believing in the prophets. This ruling is taken from al-Hidayah, emphasizing that the intention is general and not numerically determined.

Key Terms
نية الإمام (niyyat al-imam): The imam's intention to lead the prayer for the congregation, including men, women, children, and angels.
الحفظة (al-hafazah): Guardian angels who record deeds and protect humans, also participate in congregational prayer.
الخناثى (al-khunatha): Hermaphrodite or person of ambiguous gender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The imam's intention for the congregation is sunnah and should include all followers, including angels, without specifying a number for angels due to differing reports.

The Prohibition of Speech in Prayer and the Istihsan Exception
Explains prohibition of speech and istihsan exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speech during prayer and explain the istihsan exception for what cannot be asked of humans.

Core Idea
Speech in prayer is haram, but asking Allah for what humans cannot give is permitted by istihsan.

This lesson examines the foundational hadith prohibiting human speech in prayer and the Hanafi istihsan that allows certain supplications. Understanding this ruling clarifies why a worshipper can make du'a in the last sitting but cannot converse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Locate the statement that speech of people is prohibited in prayer. Note the hadith cited: 'Indeed this prayer of ours does not admit anything of people's speech.'
The negation 'la yasluhu' is a strong prohibition.
2
Contrast with the supplication hadith
The text places the speech hadith over the hadith allowing choice of du'a because the former is a 'mane' (preventer) and the latter is a 'mubih' (permitter). Understand the principle: a preventer takes precedence.
3
Define 'what resembles people's speech'
Hanafi jurists explain: requests that are possible to make of a human being (e.g., 'give me a position', 'marry me') are considered speech of people and thus prohibited. Requests impossible for humans (e.g., 'forgive me', 'grant paradise') are not speech and are allowed.
This is the istihsan exception, as noted in al-Diraya and al-Idah.

Speech of people, and turning right then left with the two taslims. And the intention of the imam for the men and the guardians. (Speech of people) due to his saying: 'Indeed this prayer of ours does not admit anything of people's speech.' And what is not impossible to ask from them is from their speech, and this is given precedence over the hadith: 'Then let each of you choose from supplication the one most pleasing to him and supplicate with it' because it is a preventer and this is a permitter, and our companions interpreted what resembles people's speech as what is not impossible to ask from other than Allah, like saying: give me such and such position, marry me to so-and-so, provide me with a concubine, and what is impossible like pardon, well-being, and forgiveness – as in al-Diraya from al-Idah. (And) it is sunnah to turn right then left with the two taslims because he (peace be upon him) used to say salam from his right saying: 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah' until the whiteness of his right cheek was seen, and from his left: 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah' until the whiteness of his left cheek was seen – narrated by the authors of Sunan and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. And the sunnah is to lower his voice in the second taslim compared to the first. The most perfect you have known from his noble wording. If he says 'al-Salamu alaykum' or 'al-Salam' or 'Salamun alaykum' or 'Alaykum al-Salam' it suffices him, but he has abandoned the sunnah, and it is explicitly stated in al-Siraj that the last is disliked, and that he should not say 'wa barakatuh', and al-Nawawi explicitly stated it is an innovation) and there is nothing [established] in it. So if he starts with his left intentionally or forgetfully, he says salam from his right and does not repeat it on his left, and nothing is upon him. If he says salam straight ahead, then he says salam from his left. If he forgets the left until he stands up, he returns and sits and says salam as long as he has not spoken or left the mosque. (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the imam for the men) and those with him from the effeminate and boys (and the guardians). Hafazah is the plural of hafiz, like kathabah plural of katib, so named for their preservation of what issues from a person of speech and action, or for preserving him from jinn and causes of perdition), and he does not intend a limited number because the reports about their number have differed, so it resembles belief in the prophets, peace be upon them – as in al-Hidayah. It is said: the noble scribes are two, one on his right and one on his left. From Ibn Abbas that he said: 'With every believer there are five of the guardians: one on his right writes the good deeds, one on his left writes the sins, another before him suggests good deeds, another behind him repels calamities, another at his forelock writes what he sends of blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and conveys it to the Messenger.' And in some reports: 'With every believer there are sixty angels, and in some: one hundred sixty, they protect him as the weak women are protected from flies on a summer day. If they were revealed to you, you would see them on every plain and mountain, each with hand outstretched, mouth open. And if the servant were left to himself for the blink of an eye, the devils would snatch him away.' So belief in them is like belief in the prophets, because their number is not definitively known, so he should say: I believe in Allah, His angels, and all the prophets, the first of them Adam and the last of them Muhammad (peace be upon him). And it is said: the number of prophets is one hundred twenty thousand. (And) his intention (for the righteous jinn) who follow him, so the imam intends all (with the two taslims, in the most correct opinion) because he addresses them so he intends them in both. It is said: he does not intend because he gestures to them. It is said: he intends with the first taslim. (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the follower for his imam in his direction) – the right if he is there, or left if he is there. (And if he faces him, he intends him in the two taslims) because he has a share from every direction, and he is more entitled than the attendees because he has done good to the follower by undertaking his prayer (with the congregation, the guardians, and the righteous jinn). (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the one praying alone for the angels only) since there is no one else with him. And one should pay attention to this, for few scholars pay attention to it, let alone others. (And) it is sunnah (to lower the second taslim compared to the first) – we have already presented its explanation. (And) it is sunnah (his accompanying) i.e. the follower's salam (with the salam of the imam) according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions, it is after the imam's salam. Following is in agreement with the Quran, and this is a second narration from the Imam. According to the other narration, which is 'Zahir al-Riwayah', there is no need to differentiate between it and the opening takbir for accompaniment in both. According to other than 'Zahir al-Riwayah', the difference is that accompanying the takbir is haste towards worship, whereas accompanying the salam is haste towards exiting prayer and engaging in worldly matters, and the former is desirable while the latter is not – as in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. (And) it is sunnah (to start with the right) – we have already explained it. (And) it is sunnah (for the one who has been preceded to wait for the imam to finish) due to the obligation of following, and he should not hasten to stand until he knows that there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon the imam. We will mention its completion, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the sunnah acts related to the final salutations (taslim) in prayer. It begins by reiterating that speaking to people during prayer is prohibited, citing the authentic hadith that prayer does not admit any human speech. The author clarifies that any request that could be made of a human being is considered speech, and this takes precedence over the hadith allowing choice of supplication in the last sitting because the prohibition is stronger (a preventer vs. a permitter). The Hanafi jurists interpret 'speech resembling people's talk' as requests that are possible to ask of anyone except Allah, such as asking for a position or marriage, while requests that are impossible for humans (like forgiveness) are permissible. Then the sunnah of turning right and left for the two taslims is mentioned, supported by the hadith describing the Prophet's practice. The preferred way is to say 'al-Salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' while turning the head so that the cheek is visible. The second taslim should be said in a lower voice than the first. Variations like just 'al-Salam' or 'Salamun alaykum' are sufficient but miss the sunnah. Saying 'Alaykum al-Salam' is disliked, and adding 'wa barakatuh' is considered an innovation by some scholars. If one mistakenly starts with the left, he should still give salam to the right and not repeat the left. If he forgets the left until after standing, he should return and do it as long as he hasn't spoken or left. Next, the intention of the imam when saying taslim is discussed. The imam should intend the male worshippers (including effeminate men and boys) and the guardian angels (hafazah). The number of angels is not specified, so belief in them is like belief in the prophets—on general faith. Some reports mention two scribes, five guardians, sixty or one hundred sixty angels. The imam should also intend righteous jinn who are following the prayer, according to the most correct view, because they are addressed in the taslim. The follower intends his imam in the direction he is (right, left, or facing), along with the congregation, angels, and righteous jinn. The one praying alone intends only the angels, as no one else is present. The follower should accompany the imam's salam according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it should be after. The relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah) is that there is no distinction between taslim and takbir in this regard—both can be done simultaneously. The sunnah is to start the taslim to the right, and a latecomer should wait for the imam to complete all taslims before standing up, in case there is a prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). The passage thus covers a comprehensive set of recommended practices for concluding the prayer.

Key Terms
كلام الناس (kalām al-nās): Human speech that is prohibited during prayer
مانع (māni'): A preventer; here, a proof that prohibits

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following supplications during prayer would be considered prohibited speech according to the Hanafi school?
A) 'O Allah, forgive me.'
B) 'O Allah, grant me a house in this world.'
C) 'O Allah, have mercy on my parents.'
D) 'O Allah, admit me to Paradise.'

Key Takeaway
Speech in prayer is haram, but asking Allah for what only He can grant is permissible due to istihsan.

The Sunnah of Turning and the Manner of Taslim
Explains the sunnah of turning and phrasing in taslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah manner of performing the taslim, including the turning, phrasing, and handling mistakes.

Core Idea
Turning right then left with 'al-Salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' is sunnah, and variations are valid but miss the sunnah.

This lesson details the recommended acts for the closing salutations, based on the Prophet's practice. Understanding these sunan helps one perfect the prayer while knowing what suffices in necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah of turning
The text states it is sunnah to turn right then left while saying the two taslims. Note the hadith describing the Prophet's practice: turning until his cheek was visible.
Turning is a sunnah, not a fard or wajib.
2
List the sunnah wording
The sunnah is to say 'al-Salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' on each side. The text also mentions saying 'al-Salamu alaykum', 'al-Salam', 'Salamun alaykum' are sufficient but miss the sunnah. 'Alaykum al-Salam' is disliked.
Adding 'wa barakatuh' is considered an innovation.
3
Analyze mistakes and corrections
If one starts with the left side, he should still give salam on the right and not repeat the left. If he forgets the left until after standing, he returns and does it as long as he hasn't spoken or left the mosque.
These rulings cover forgetfulness and error.

Source Text

( كَلامِ النَّاسِ) لقوله : ( إِنَّ صَلَاتَنَا هَذِهِ لا يَصْلُحُ فِيهَا شَيْءٌ مِنْ كَلامِ النَّاسِ ). وما لا يستحيل سؤاله منهم فهو من كلامهم، وهذا مقدم على حديث: «ثُمَّ يَتَخَيَّرُ أحَدُكُمْ مِنْ الدُّعَاءِ أَعْجَبَهُ إِلَيْهِ فَيَدْعُو بِهِ »، لأنه مانع وهذا مبيح، وفسّر أصحابنا ما يشبه كلام الناس بما لا يستحيل سؤالـه مـن غير الله تعالى، كقولك: أعطني منصب كذا، زوجني فلانة، وارزقني سرية سنية، وما يستحيل كالعفو والعافية والغفران كذا في «الدراية». عن «الإيضاح». (وَ) يسن (نيّة الإمام الرِّجال) ومن معه من ) والخنائي والصبيان ( والحفظة). جمع حافظ، ككتبة جمع كاتب، وسموا به لحفظهم ما يصدر من الإنسان من قول وعمل، أو لحفظهم إياه من الجن وأسباب المعاطب ) ، ولا ينوي عدداً محصوراً، لأن الأخبار في عددهم قد اختلفت فأشبه الإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام كذا في « الهداية ». قيل: الكرام الكاتبين، اثنان، واحد عن يمينه وواحد عن يساره، وعن ابن عباس أنه قال: « مَـعْ كُـلّ مُؤْمِن خَمْسٌ مِنَ الحَفَظَةِ: واحِدٌ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ يَكْتُبُ الحَسَنَاتِ، وواحِدٌ عَنْ يَسَارِهِ يَكْتُبُ السَّيِّئَاتِ، وَآخَرُ أمَامَهُ يُلَقِّنُهُ الخيراتِ، وآخَرُ ورَاءهُ يَدْفَعُ عَنْهُ المَكَارِة، وآخَرُ عِنْدَ نَاصِيَتِهِ يَكْتُبُ مَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويبلغه إلى الرَّسُولَ عليه الصلاة والسلام ) ) . وفي بعض الأخبار : « مــع كــل مـؤمـن سـتـون ملكاً، وفي بعضها: مائة وستون يذبون عنهُ كَمَا يُذَبُ عن ضعفة النساء في اليـوم الـصـائف الذباب، ولو بدوا لكُم لرأيتموهم على كلّ سهل وجبل كلّهم باسط يده فاغر فَاه، ولو وكل العبد إلى نفسه طرفة عين لاختطفته الشياطين () () ، فالإيمانُ بِهمْ، كالإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، لأن عددهم ليس بمعلوم قـ م قطعاً، فينبغي أن يقول : آمنت بالله وملائكته، وجميع الأنبياء أولهـم آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وآخرهم محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم. وقيل: عدد الأنبياء مائة وعشرون ألفاً. (وَ) نيته (صَالِحَ الجِنِّ) المقتدين به فينوي الإمام الجميع (بالتسليمتين، في الأصح)، لأنه يخاطبهم فينويهم فيهما، وقيل: لا ينوي لأنه يشير إليهم، وقيل: ينوي بالتسليمة الأولى. (و) يسن (نيّةُ المأموم إمامَهُ في جِهَتِهِ) اليمين إن كان فيها، أو اليسار إن كان فيها، وإنْ حَاذَاهُ نَوَاهُ في التَسْلِيمَتَين)، لأن له حظاً من كل جهة، وهـو أحق من الحاضرين، لأنه أحسن إلى المأموم بالتزام صلاته (مَعَ القَوْمِ، وَالحَفَظَةِ، وصَالِحِ الجِنِّ). (و) يسن (نيَّة المنفردِ الملائكة، فَقَط، إذ ليس معه غيرهم وينبغي التنبه لهذا، فإنه قل من يتنبه لــه من أهل العلم فضلاً عن غيرهم. (وَ) يسن (خَفْضُ) التسليمة ( الثانية عن التسليمة (الأولى) وقدمناه شرحاً (وَ) يسن (مُقَارَنَتُهُ) أي: سلام المقتدي (لِسَلامِ الإِمَامِ) عند الإمام، وعندهما بعد تسليم الإمام والاقتداء موافقة بالقرآن، وهي رواية ثانية عن الإمام، وعلى الرواية الأخرى، وهـي «ظاهر الرواية» لا يحتاج إلى فرق بينها وبين التحريمة للمقارنة فيهما، وعلى غير «ظاهر الرواية»، الفرق هو أن مقارنة التكبير سرعة إلى العبادة، وفي مقارنة التسليم سرعة إلى الخروج عن الصلاة والاشتغال بأمور الدنيا، والأول مطلوب دون الثاني، كذا في « التجنيس والمزيد ». (وَ) يســــن ( البُدَاءةُ بِاليَمِينِ) وقد بيناه)، (وَ) يسن ( انتظار المسبوق فراغ الإمام) لوجوب المتابعة، ولا يعجل بالقيام حتى يعلم أن لا . سجود سهو على الإمام، وسنذكر تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى.
Speech of people, and turning right then left with the two taslims. And the intention of the imam for the men and the guardians. (Speech of people) due to his saying: 'Indeed this prayer of ours does not admit anything of people's speech.' And what is not impossible to ask from them is from their speech, and this is given precedence over the hadith: 'Then let each of you choose from supplication the one most pleasing to him and supplicate with it' because it is a preventer and this is a permitter, and our companions interpreted what resembles people's speech as what is not impossible to ask from other than Allah, like saying: give me such and such position, marry me to so-and-so, provide me with a concubine, and what is impossible like pardon, well-being, and forgiveness – as in al-Diraya from al-Idah. (And) it is sunnah to turn right then left with the two taslims because he (peace be upon him) used to say salam from his right saying: 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah' until the whiteness of his right cheek was seen, and from his left: 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah' until the whiteness of his left cheek was seen – narrated by the authors of Sunan and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. And the sunnah is to lower his voice in the second taslim compared to the first. The most perfect you have known from his noble wording. If he says 'al-Salamu alaykum' or 'al-Salam' or 'Salamun alaykum' or 'Alaykum al-Salam' it suffices him, but he has abandoned the sunnah, and it is explicitly stated in al-Siraj that the last is disliked, and that he should not say 'wa barakatuh', and al-Nawawi explicitly stated it is an innovation) and there is nothing [established] in it. So if he starts with his left intentionally or forgetfully, he says salam from his right and does not repeat it on his left, and nothing is upon him. If he says salam straight ahead, then he says salam from his left. If he forgets the left until he stands up, he returns and sits and says salam as long as he has not spoken or left the mosque. (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the imam for the men) and those with him from the effeminate and boys (and the guardians). Hafazah is the plural of hafiz, like kathabah plural of katib, so named for their preservation of what issues from a person of speech and action, or for preserving him from jinn and causes of perdition), and he does not intend a limited number because the reports about their number have differed, so it resembles belief in the prophets, peace be upon them – as in al-Hidayah. It is said: the noble scribes are two, one on his right and one on his left. From Ibn Abbas that he said: 'With every believer there are five of the guardians: one on his right writes the good deeds, one on his left writes the sins, another before him suggests good deeds, another behind him repels calamities, another at his forelock writes what he sends of blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and conveys it to the Messenger.' And in some reports: 'With every believer there are sixty angels, and in some: one hundred sixty, they protect him as the weak women are protected from flies on a summer day. If they were revealed to you, you would see them on every plain and mountain, each with hand outstretched, mouth open. And if the servant were left to himself for the blink of an eye, the devils would snatch him away.' So belief in them is like belief in the prophets, because their number is not definitively known, so he should say: I believe in Allah, His angels, and all the prophets, the first of them Adam and the last of them Muhammad (peace be upon him). And it is said: the number of prophets is one hundred twenty thousand. (And) his intention (for the righteous jinn) who follow him, so the imam intends all (with the two taslims, in the most correct opinion) because he addresses them so he intends them in both. It is said: he does not intend because he gestures to them. It is said: he intends with the first taslim. (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the follower for his imam in his direction) – the right if he is there, or left if he is there. (And if he faces him, he intends him in the two taslims) because he has a share from every direction, and he is more entitled than the attendees because he has done good to the follower by undertaking his prayer (with the congregation, the guardians, and the righteous jinn). (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the one praying alone for the angels only) since there is no one else with him. And one should pay attention to this, for few scholars pay attention to it, let alone others. (And) it is sunnah (to lower the second taslim compared to the first) – we have already presented its explanation. (And) it is sunnah (his accompanying) i.e. the follower's salam (with the salam of the imam) according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions, it is after the imam's salam. Following is in agreement with the Quran, and this is a second narration from the Imam. According to the other narration, which is 'Zahir al-Riwayah', there is no need to differentiate between it and the opening takbir for accompaniment in both. According to other than 'Zahir al-Riwayah', the difference is that accompanying the takbir is haste towards worship, whereas accompanying the salam is haste towards exiting prayer and engaging in worldly matters, and the former is desirable while the latter is not – as in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. (And) it is sunnah (to start with the right) – we have already explained it. (And) it is sunnah (for the one who has been preceded to wait for the imam to finish) due to the obligation of following, and he should not hasten to stand until he knows that there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon the imam. We will mention its completion, Allah willing.

Key Terms
التفات (iltifāt): Turning the head to the right and left during taslim
بدعة (bid'ah): Innovation in religion; here, adding 'wa barakatuh' is considered bid'ah by some scholars.

Which of the following is considered a disliked (makruh) variation of the taslim according to the Hanafi school?

Salah — Prayer
advanced
15 min
The Intentions (Niyyah) in Taslim and Rulings for Follower and Munfarid
Explains the intentions in taslim and additional sunan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended intentions for imam, follower, and one praying alone when saying taslim, and apply the rulings on follower's timing and waiting for imam.

Core Idea
The imam intends men, angels, and righteous jinn; the follower intends his imam, congregation, angels, and jinn; the one alone intends only angels.

This lesson covers the niyyah (intention) made during taslim and the associated sunan for follower and munfarid. Understanding these intentions deepens the act of concluding prayer and clarifies the follower's role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's intention
The imam should intend the male worshippers (including effeminate men and boys), the guardian angels (hafazah), and the righteous jinn. The text notes that the number of angels is not specified, so belief in them is general.
Intention is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Identify the follower's intention
The follower intends his imam in the direction he is (right, left, or facing), along with the congregation, angels, and righteous jinn.
The imam is more entitled than others.
3
Identify the intention of the one praying alone
The munfarid intends only the angels, as there are no humans or jinn present.
This is often overlooked, even by scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلام الناس، والالتفات يميناً، ثمّ يساراً، بالتسليمتين. ونيّةُ الإمام الرِّجالَ، والحَفَظَةَ . ( كَلامِ النَّاسِ) لقوله : ( إِنَّ صَلَاتَنَا هَذِهِ لا يَصْلُحُ فِيهَا شَيْءٌ مِنْ كَلامِ النَّاسِ ). وما لا يستحيل سؤاله منهم فهو من كلامهم، وهذا مقدم على حديث: «ثُمَّ يَتَخَيَّرُ أحَدُكُمْ مِنْ الدُّعَاءِ أَعْجَبَهُ إِلَيْهِ فَيَدْعُو بِهِ »، لأنه مانع وهذا مبيح، وفسّر أصحابنا ما يشبه كلام الناس بما لا يستحيل سؤالـه مـن غير الله تعالى، كقولك: أعطني منصب كذا، زوجني فلانة، وارزقني سرية سنية، وما يستحيل كالعفو والعافية والغفران كذا في «الدراية». عن «الإيضاح». (وَ) يسن (الالتفات يميناً، ثـم يـسـاراً، بالتسليمتين) لأنه ( كَانَ يُسَلِّمُ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ فَيَقُولُ: السَّلامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ، حَتَّى يُرَى بَيَاضُ حَدِّهِ الْأَيْمَنِ وَعَنْ يَسَارِهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ حَتَّى يُرَى بَيَاضُ خَدِّهِ الأَيْسَرِ » رواه أصحاب السنن وصححه الترمذي، والسنة أن يخفض صوته في الثانية عن الأولى والأكمل قد علمته من لفظه الشريف فإن قال: السلام عليكم أو السلام، أو سلام عليكم، أو عليكم السلام أجزأه، وكان تاركاً للسنة، وصرح به في «السراج» بكراهة الأخير، وأنه لا يقول وبركاته، وصرح النووي بأنه بدعة)، وليس فيه [ شيء ] ثابت، فلو بدأ بيساره عامداً، أو ناسياً يسلم عن يمينه، ولا يعيده عـلـى يـســاره، ولا شيء عليه، ولو سلم تلقاء وجهه، فإنه يسلم عن يساره، ولو نسي يساره حتى قام يرجع ويقعد ويسلم ما لم يتكلم، أو يخرج من المسجد ). (وَ) يسن (نيّة الإمام الرِّجال) ومن معه من ) والخنائي والصبيان ( والحفظة). جمع حافظ، ككتبة جمع كاتب، وسموا به لحفظهم ما يصدر من الإنسان من قول وعمل، أو لحفظهم إياه من الجن وأسباب المعاطب ) ، ولا ينوي عدداً محصوراً، لأن الأخبار في عددهم قد اختلفت فأشبه الإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام كذا في « الهداية ». قيل: الكرام الكاتبين، اثنان، واحد عن يمينه وواحد عن يساره، وعن ابن عباس أنه قال: « مَـعْ كُـلّ مُؤْمِن خَمْسٌ مِنَ الحَفَظَةِ: واحِدٌ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ يَكْتُبُ الحَسَنَاتِ، وواحِدٌ عَنْ يَسَارِهِ يَكْتُبُ السَّيِّئَاتِ، وَآخَرُ أمَامَهُ يُلَقِّنُهُ الخيراتِ، وآخَرُ ورَاءهُ يَدْفَعُ عَنْهُ المَكَارِة، وآخَرُ عِنْدَ نَاصِيَتِهِ يَكْتُبُ مَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويبلغه إلى الرَّسُولَ عليه الصلاة والسلام ) ) . وفي بعض الأخبار : « مــع كــل مـؤمـن سـتـون ملكاً، وفي بعضها: مائة وستون يذبون عنهُ كَمَا يُذَبُ عن ضعفة النساء في اليـوم الـصـائف الذباب، ولو بدوا لكُم لرأيتموهم على كلّ سهل وجبل كلّهم باسط يده فاغر فَاه، ولو وكل العبد إلى نفسه طرفة عين لاختطفته الشياطين () () ، فالإيمانُ بِهمْ، كالإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، لأن عددهم ليس بمعلوم قـ م قطعاً، فينبغي أن يقول : آمنت بالله وملائكته، وجميع الأنبياء أولهـم آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وآخرهم محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم. وقيل: عدد الأنبياء مائة وعشرون ألفاً. (وَ) نيته (صَالِحَ الجِنِّ) المقتدين به فينوي الإمام الجميع (بالتسليمتين، في الأصح)، لأنه يخاطبهم فينويهم فيهما، وقيل: لا ينوي لأنه يشير إليهم، وقيل: ينوي بالتسليمة الأولى. (و) يسن (نيّةُ المأموم إمامَهُ في جِهَتِهِ) اليمين إن كان فيها، أو اليسار إن كان فيها، وإنْ حَاذَاهُ نَوَاهُ في التَسْلِيمَتَين)، لأن له حظاً من كل جهة، وهـو أحق من الحاضرين، لأنه أحسن إلى المأموم بالتزام صلاته (مَعَ القَوْمِ، وَالحَفَظَةِ، وصَالِحِ الجِنِّ). (و) يسن (نيَّة المنفردِ الملائكة، فَقَط، إذ ليس معه غيرهم وينبغي التنبه لهذا، فإنه قل من يتنبه لــه من أهل العلم فضلاً عن غيرهم. (وَ) يسن (خَفْضُ) التسليمة ( الثانية عن التسليمة (الأولى) وقدمناه شرحاً (وَ) يسن (مُقَارَنَتُهُ) أي: سلام المقتدي (لِسَلامِ الإِمَامِ) عند الإمام، وعندهما بعد تسليم الإمام والاقتداء موافقة بالقرآن، وهي رواية ثانية عن الإمام، وعلى الرواية الأخرى، وهـي «ظاهر الرواية» لا يحتاج إلى فرق بينها وبين التحريمة للمقارنة فيهما، وعلى غير «ظاهر الرواية»، الفرق هو أن مقارنة التكبير سرعة إلى العبادة، وفي مقارنة التسليم سرعة إلى الخروج عن الصلاة والاشتغال بأمور الدنيا، والأول مطلوب دون الثاني، كذا في « التجنيس والمزيد ». (وَ) يســــن ( البُدَاءةُ بِاليَمِينِ) وقد بيناه)، (وَ) يسن ( انتظار المسبوق فراغ الإمام) لوجوب المتابعة، ولا يعجل بالقيام حتى يعلم أن لا . سجود سهو على الإمام، وسنذكر تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى.
Speech of people, and turning right then left with the two taslims. And the intention of the imam for the men and the guardians. (Speech of people) due to his saying: 'Indeed this prayer of ours does not admit anything of people's speech.' And what is not impossible to ask from them is from their speech, and this is given precedence over the hadith: 'Then let each of you choose from supplication the one most pleasing to him and supplicate with it' because it is a preventer and this is a permitter, and our companions interpreted what resembles people's speech as what is not impossible to ask from other than Allah, like saying: give me such and such position, marry me to so-and-so, provide me with a concubine, and what is impossible like pardon, well-being, and forgiveness – as in al-Diraya from al-Idah. (And) it is sunnah to turn right then left with the two taslims because he (peace be upon him) used to say salam from his right saying: 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah' until the whiteness of his right cheek was seen, and from his left: 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah' until the whiteness of his left cheek was seen – narrated by the authors of Sunan and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. And the sunnah is to lower his voice in the second taslim compared to the first. The most perfect you have known from his noble wording. If he says 'al-Salamu alaykum' or 'al-Salam' or 'Salamun alaykum' or 'Alaykum al-Salam' it suffices him, but he has abandoned the sunnah, and it is explicitly stated in al-Siraj that the last is disliked, and that he should not say 'wa barakatuh', and al-Nawawi explicitly stated it is an innovation) and there is nothing [established] in it. So if he starts with his left intentionally or forgetfully, he says salam from his right and does not repeat it on his left, and nothing is upon him. If he says salam straight ahead, then he says salam from his left. If he forgets the left until he stands up, he returns and sits and says salam as long as he has not spoken or left the mosque. (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the imam for the men) and those with him from the effeminate and boys (and the guardians). Hafazah is the plural of hafiz, like kathabah plural of katib, so named for their preservation of what issues from a person of speech and action, or for preserving him from jinn and causes of perdition), and he does not intend a limited number because the reports about their number have differed, so it resembles belief in the prophets, peace be upon them – as in al-Hidayah. It is said: the noble scribes are two, one on his right and one on his left. From Ibn Abbas that he said: 'With every believer there are five of the guardians: one on his right writes the good deeds, one on his left writes the sins, another before him suggests good deeds, another behind him repels calamities, another at his forelock writes what he sends of blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and conveys it to the Messenger.' And in some reports: 'With every believer there are sixty angels, and in some: one hundred sixty, they protect him as the weak women are protected from flies on a summer day. If they were revealed to you, you would see them on every plain and mountain, each with hand outstretched, mouth open. And if the servant were left to himself for the blink of an eye, the devils would snatch him away.' So belief in them is like belief in the prophets, because their number is not definitively known, so he should say: I believe in Allah, His angels, and all the prophets, the first of them Adam and the last of them Muhammad (peace be upon him). And it is said: the number of prophets is one hundred twenty thousand. (And) his intention (for the righteous jinn) who follow him, so the imam intends all (with the two taslims, in the most correct opinion) because he addresses them so he intends them in both. It is said: he does not intend because he gestures to them. It is said: he intends with the first taslim. (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the follower for his imam in his direction) – the right if he is there, or left if he is there. (And if he faces him, he intends him in the two taslims) because he has a share from every direction, and he is more entitled than the attendees because he has done good to the follower by undertaking his prayer (with the congregation, the guardians, and the righteous jinn). (And) it is sunnah (the intention of the one praying alone for the angels only) since there is no one else with him. And one should pay attention to this, for few scholars pay attention to it, let alone others. (And) it is sunnah (to lower the second taslim compared to the first) – we have already presented its explanation. (And) it is sunnah (his accompanying) i.e. the follower's salam (with the salam of the imam) according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions, it is after the imam's salam. Following is in agreement with the Quran, and this is a second narration from the Imam. According to the other narration, which is 'Zahir al-Riwayah', there is no need to differentiate between it and the opening takbir for accompaniment in both. According to other than 'Zahir al-Riwayah', the difference is that accompanying the takbir is haste towards worship, whereas accompanying the salam is haste towards exiting prayer and engaging in worldly matters, and the former is desirable while the latter is not – as in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. (And) it is sunnah (to start with the right) – we have already explained it. (And) it is sunnah (for the one who has been preceded to wait for the imam to finish) due to the obligation of following, and he should not hasten to stand until he knows that there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon the imam. We will mention its completion, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the sunnah acts related to the final salutations (taslim) in prayer. It begins by reiterating that speaking to people during prayer is prohibited, citing the authentic hadith that prayer does not admit any human speech. The author clarifies that any request that could be made of a human being is considered speech, and this takes precedence over the hadith allowing choice of supplication in the last sitting because the prohibition is stronger (a preventer vs. a permitter). The Hanafi jurists interpret 'speech resembling people's talk' as requests that are possible to ask of anyone except Allah, such as asking for a position or marriage, while requests that are impossible for humans (like forgiveness) are permissible. Then the sunnah of turning right and left for the two taslims is mentioned, supported by the hadith describing the Prophet's practice. The preferred way is to say 'al-Salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' while turning the head so that the cheek is visible. The second taslim should be said in a lower voice than the first. Variations like just 'al-Salam' or 'Salamun alaykum' are sufficient but miss the sunnah. Saying 'Alaykum al-Salam' is disliked, and adding 'wa barakatuh' is considered an innovation by some scholars. If one mistakenly starts with the left, he should still give salam to the right and not repeat the left. If he forgets the left until after standing, he should return and do it as long as he hasn't spoken or left. Next, the intention of the imam when saying taslim is discussed. The imam should intend the male worshippers (including effeminate men and boys) and the guardian angels (hafazah). The number of angels is not specified, so belief in them is like belief in the prophets—on general faith. Some reports mention two scribes, five guardians, sixty or one hundred sixty angels. The imam should also intend righteous jinn who are following the prayer, according to the most correct view, because they are addressed in the taslim. The follower intends his imam in the direction he is (right, left, or facing), along with the congregation, angels, and righteous jinn. The one praying alone intends only the angels, as no one else is present. The follower should accompany the imam's salam according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it should be after. The relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah) is that there is no distinction between taslim and takbir in this regard—both can be done simultaneously. The sunnah is to start the taslim to the right, and a latecomer should wait for the imam to complete all taslims before standing up, in case there is a prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). The passage thus covers a comprehensive set of recommended practices for concluding the prayer.

Key Terms
حفظة (ḥafaẓah): Guardian angels; the imam intends them in taslim.
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joined the prayer late and missed some rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view (al-ashah), when should the imam intend the righteous jinn in his taslim?
A) Only in the first taslim
B) Only in the second taslim
C) In both taslims
D) Not at all

Key Takeaway
Intention in taslim is sunnah; the imam intends men, angels, and jinn; the follower intends the imam and others; the alone intends only angels.
