Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Intentions for the Salutation of Peace (Salam)
Rulings on intention for the salam in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended intentions for the imam, follower, and individual during the salam and explain the difference of opinion regarding synchronization.

Core Idea
Your salam greets not only those beside you, but also the angels and righteous jinn.

This passage from Nur al-Idah details the sunnah intentions for the final salutation of peace (salam) in prayer. It covers the imam, follower, and individual, and includes a critical difference of opinion on whether the follower synchronizes with or follows the imam's salam. Understanding these intentions completes the prayer with mindfulness and aligns with the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of worshippers
The passage distinguishes three roles: imam, follower (muqtadi), and individual (munfarid). For each, there is a specific set of entities to intend in the salam.
The masbuq (latecomer) is a fourth category with its own ruling later.
2
List the entities to intend for each role
For the imam: congregation, guardian angels, and righteous jinn (with both salutations). For the follower: his imam in the direction, plus congregation, angels, and righteous jinn. For the individual: only the angels.
The most correct view is that the imam intends the righteous jinn with both salutations.
3
Note the additional sunan
Besides intention, the text lists: lowering the second salutation, starting with the right, and for the masbuq, waiting for the imam to fully finish.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on synchronization
Abu Hanifa holds that the follower synchronizes his salam with the imam, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say to salute after. The apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) equates it to takbir, but later scholars prefer the follower saluting after.
The practical difference: if the follower synchronizes, he ends prayer simultaneously; if after, he ends slightly later.
5
Apply the ruling for the masbuq
The masbuq must wait for the imam to complete both salutations and any necessary sajdah al-sahw before standing to complete his own prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصالح الجن، بالتسليمتين، في الأصح. وليّة المأموم إمامَهُ في جهته، وإنْ حَاذَاهُ نواه في التسليمتين مع القوم، والحَفَظَةِ، وصالح الجن، وليه المنفردِ الملائكة فقط. وخَفْصُ الثانية عن الأولى، ومُقَارَنَتُهُ لسلام الإمام، والبداءة باليمين، وانتظار المسبوق فراغ الإمام. (۲) (1) قيل: الكرام الكاتبين، اثنان، واحد عن يمينه وواحد عن يساره، وعن ابن عباس أنه قال: « مَـعْ كُـلّ مُؤْمِن خَمْسٌ مِنَ الحَفَظَةِ: واحِدٌ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ يَكْتُبُ الحَسَنَاتِ، وواحِدٌ عَنْ يَسَارِهِ يَكْتُبُ السَّيِّئَاتِ، وَآخَرُ أمَامَهُ يُلَقِّنُهُ الخيراتِ، وآخَرُ ورَاءهُ يَدْفَعُ عَنْهُ المَكَارِة، وآخَرُ عِنْدَ نَاصِيَتِهِ يَكْتُبُ مَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويبلغه إلى الرَّسُولَ عليه الصلاة والسلام ) ) . وفي بعض الأخبار : « مــع كــل مـؤمـن سـتـون ملكاً، وفي بعضها: مائة وستون يذبون عنهُ كَمَا يُذَبُ عن ضعفة النساء في اليـوم الـصـائف الذباب، ولو بدوا لكُم لرأيتموهم على كلّ سهل وجبل كلّهم باسط يده فاغر فاه، ولو وكل العبد إلى نفسه طرفة عين لاختطفته الشياطين () () ، فالإيمانُ بِهمْ، كالإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، لأن عددهم ليس بمعلوم قط، فينبغي أن يقول : آمنت بالله وملائكته، وجميع الأنبياء أولهـم آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وآخرهم محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم. وقيل: عدد الأنبياء مائة وعشرون ألفاً. (وَ) نيته (صَالِحَ الجِنِّ) المقتدين به فينوي الإمام الجميع (بالتسليمتين، في الأصح)، لأنه يخاطبهم فينويهم فيهما، وقيل: لا ينوي لأنه يشير إليهم، وقيل: ينوي بالتسليمة الأولى. (و) يسن (نيّةُ المأموم إمامَهُ في جِهَتِهِ) اليمين إن كان فيها، أو اليسار إن كان فيها، وإنْ حَاذَاهُ نَوَاهُ في التَسْلِيمَتَين)، لأن له حظاً من كل جهة، وهـو أحق من الحاضرين، لأنه أحسن إلى المأموم بالتزام صلاته (مَعَ القَوْمِ، وَالحَفَظَةِ، وصَالِحِ الجِنِّ). (و) يسن (نيَّة المنفردِ الملائكة، فَقَط، إذ ليس معه غيرهم وينبغي التنبه لهذا، فإنه قل من يتنبه لــه من أهل العلم فضلاً عن غيرهم. (وَ) يسن (خَفْضُ) التسليمة ( الثانية عن التسليمة (الأولى) وقدمناه شرحاً (وَ) يسن (مُقَارَنَتُهُ) أي: سلام المقتدي (لِسَلامِ الإِمَامِ) عند الإمام، وعندهما بعد تسليم الإمام والاقتداء موافقة بالقرآن، وهي رواية ثانية عن الإمام، وعلى الرواية الأخرى، وهـي «ظاهر الرواية» لا يحتاج إلى فرق بينها وبين التحريمة للمقارنة فيهما، وعلى غير «ظاهر الرواية»، الفرق هو أن مقارنة التكبير سرعة إلى العبادة، وفي مقارنة التسليم سرعة إلى الخروج عن الصلاة والاشتغال بأمور الدنيا، والأول مطلوب دون الثاني، كذا في « التجنيس والمزيد ». (و) يســــن ( البُدَاءةُ بِاليَمِينِ) وقد بيناه)، (وَ) يسن ( انتظار المسبوق فراغ الإمام) لوجوب المتابعة، ولا يعجل بالقيام حتى يعلم أن لا سجود سهو على الإمام، وسنذكر تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى.
And (intending) the righteous jinn with both salutations, in the most correct view. And it is sunnah for the follower to intend his imam in his direction, and if he is opposite him, he intends him in both salutations along with the congregation, the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn. And the individual intends only the angels. And lowering the second salutation compared to the first, and synchronizing his salutation with the imam's salutation, and starting with the right, and the masbuq waiting for the imam to finish. (2)(1) It was said: the noble scribes are two, one on his right and one on his left. And from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'With every believer there are five guardian angels: one on his right writes the good deeds, one on his left writes the evil deeds, another in front of him inspires him with good deeds, another behind him repels misfortunes from him, and another at his forelock writes what he sends prayers upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and conveys it to the Messenger (peace be upon him).' And in some reports: 'With every believer there are sixty angels', and in some: 'one hundred and sixty, they protect him as the weak women are protected from flies on a hot day, and if they appeared to you, you would see them on every plain and mountain, all with hands outstretched and mouths open, and if the servant were entrusted to himself for the blink of an eye, the devils would snatch him away.' So faith in them is like faith in the prophets (peace be upon them), because their number is not known definitively, so one should say: 'I believe in Allah, His angels, and all the prophets, the first of them Adam (peace be upon him) and the last of them Muhammad (peace be upon him).' And it was said: the number of prophets is one hundred and twenty thousand. (And) his intention (of the righteous jinn) who follow him, so the imam intends all of them (with both salutations, in the most correct view), because he addresses them and intends them in both; and it was said: he does not intend because he signals to them; and it was said: he intends with the first salutation. (And) it is sunnah (for the follower to intend his imam in his direction) to the right if he is there, or to the left if he is there, and if he is opposite him, he intends him in both salutations, because he has a share from each direction, and he is more deserving than those present because he has benefited the follower by undertaking his prayer. (Along with the congregation, the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn). (And) it is sunnah (for the individual to intend only the angels), since no one else is with him, and one should pay attention to this, for few scholars pay attention to it, let alone others. (And) it is sunnah (to lower) the second salutation (compared to the first) and we have already explained it. (And) it is sunnah (for him to synchronize) i.e. the follower's salutation (with the imam's salutation) according to Abu Hanifa; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) after the imam's salutation, and following is agreement in recitation, and it is a second narration from Abu Hanifa. And according to the other narration, which is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), there is no need to differentiate between it and the takbirat al-ihram regarding synchronization in both, and according to other than the apparent narration, the difference is that synchronizing the takbir is hurrying to worship, while synchronizing the salutation is hurrying to exit the prayer and engage in worldly matters; the first is desired while the second is not, as it is in 'Al-Tajnis wa Al-Mazid'. (And) it is sunnah (to start with the right) and we have explained it. (And) it is sunnah (for the masbuq to wait for the imam to finish) due to the obligation of following, and he should not hasten to stand until he knows that there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon the imam, and we will mention its completion if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the intentions (niyyah) for the salutation of peace (salam) in prayer. It covers the imam, follower, and individual. The passage begins by stating the most correct view: the imam intends the righteous jinn with both salutations. The follower intends his imam in his direction; if the imam is directly opposite, he intends him in both salutations, along with the congregation, guardian angels, and righteous jinn. The individual intending only the angels is sunnah. Additional sunnah acts include lowering the second salutation, synchronizing with the imam (with a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and the two), starting with the right, and the masbuq waiting for the imam to finish. The passage includes a lengthy hadith from Ibn Abbas about the five guardian angels assigned to every believer, and other reports about sixty or one hundred sixty angels. This serves to emphasize the reality of angels and jinn, against whom the intention is made. The text then clarifies the ruling on the imam's intention for righteous jinn: the most correct view is that he intends them with both salutations because he addresses them; alternative views are that he does not intend them because he signals, or he intends them with the first salutation only. The follower's intention for his imam is detailed: if the imam is to the right or left, he intends him in that direction; if opposite, he intends him in both salutations. The individual, having no one else present, intends only the angels. The text also discusses the issue of synchronizing the salutation: according to Abu Hanifa, the follower synchronizes with the imam's salutation; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the follower salutes after the imam. A second narration from Abu Hanifa agrees with them. The apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya) equates synchronization in salutation to that in takbir. The difference is explained: takbir is hurrying to worship, while salutation is hurrying to exit, so the former is encouraged. Finally, the masbuq must wait for the imam to finish, including any prostration of forgetfulness, before standing to complete his prayer.

Key Terms
الحفظة (al-hafazah): The guardian angels appointed to record deeds and protect the believer.
صالح الجن (salih al-jinn): The righteous jinn who follow the imam in prayer or are present.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joined the congregation late and missed one or more rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view, whom does the imam intend with both salutations?
A) Only the congregation
B) The congregation, guardian angels, and righteous jinn
C) Only the guardian angels
D) The righteous jinn only

Key Takeaway
The intention in salam is a sunnah that extends beyond humans to include angels and righteous jinn, and the follower should generally salute after the imam.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Etiquette of Prayer: Where to Look and Removing Hands from Sleeves
Defines adab (etiquette) in prayer and details specific actions for men and women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six etiquettes of gaze during prayer and the gender-specific ruling for removing hands from sleeves, and explain the Hanafi categorization of adab.

Core Idea
Adab in prayer perfects sunnah, which perfects fard; each recommended action deepens khushu.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its sharh defines adab as a distinct category of recommended actions that the Prophet performed only occasionally. It then details specific physical etiquettes: where to look in each posture and whether to remove hands from sleeves. Understanding these rulings helps us cultivate khushu (humble concentration) without assuming they are obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Define adab and its hierarchical role
The passage defines adab terminologically as actions done by the Prophet once or twice without persistence, and states that adab perfects sunnah, sunnah perfects wajib, wajib perfects fard. This shows the graded structure of Hanafi rulings.
Note that adab is not wajib or sunnah mu'akkadah; omission requires no compensation.
2
Identify the hand-placement ruling for men and women
The text states that men should remove their hands from sleeves during takbirat al-ihram to show humility, except for necessity like cold. Women should not remove their hands because it would expose their forearms, which are 'awrah.
Hermaphrodites follow the woman's rule as a precaution.
3
List the six gaze etiquettes for each posture
While standing, look at place of prostration; while bowing, look at top of feet; while prostrating, look at tip of nose; while sitting, look at lap; while greeting, look at shoulders (right then left).
Even if seeing the Ka'bah, the madhhab prefers looking at prostration place to avoid distraction.
4
Understand the underlying principle: khushu
All these etiquettes aim to foster khushu—inner humility and outer calmness of limbs. The hadith 'Worship Allah as if you see Him' is cited to reinforce the mindset.
Khushu is both in the heart and manifested physically.
5
Recognize the epistemological weight
These actions are categorized as adab, a level below sunnah, with no compensation required for omission. This distinguishes them from fard (pillars) and wajib (obligatory elements needing compensation).
Knowing the level prevents overburdening the worshipper.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل من آداب الصلاة إخراجُ الرَّجُلِ كَفَيْهِ مِنْ كُمَّيْهِ عند التكبير، ونَظَرُ المصلّي إلى موضع سجوده قائماً، وإلى ظاهر القدم راكعاً، وإلى أَرْنَبَةِ أنفه ساجداً، وإلى حجره جالساً، وإلى المنكبين مُسلماً. فصل من آداب الصلاة أشرنا بمن التبعيضية إلى أننا لم نستقص أفراد الأدب، بل ذكرنا ما تيسر منه وه، والأدب في اللغة معلوم، قال الجوهري: الأدب أدب النفس والدرس، تقول منه : أدب الرجل، فهو أديب. وأدبته فتأدب. وفي الاصطلاح هو كل ما فعله الرسول الله مرة أو مرتين، ولم يواظب عليه، كـزيــادة التسبيحات في الركوع والسجود، والزيادة على القراءة المسنونة ، كما في ( العناية»، و « الدراية»، وغيرهما. والأدب شرع لإكمال السُّنة، والسنة لإكمال الواجب، والواجب لإكمال الـفـرض. كما في البزازية، فمن آداب الصَّلاة ( إخراجُ الرَّجُلِ كَفَيْهِ مِنْ كُمَّيْهِ عِنْدَ التَّكْبير) أي: تكبير الإحرام؛ لأنه أقرب إلى التواضع، وأبعد من التشبه بالجبابرة، وأمكن من نشر الأصابع إلا لضرورة بـــرد ونحوه. ولا تخرج المرأة كفيها، لأنه يؤدي إلى كشف ساعديها، وهمـا عــورة ومبنــى حـالـهـا عـلـى الـسـتـر، والخنثى كالمرأة احتياطاً. (وَنَظَرُ المُصَلِّي ) سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة ( إلى مَوْضِعِ سُجُودِهِ قَائِمَاً ) حفظاً له عن النظر إلى ما يشغله عن الخشوع، وسنذكر أن الخشوع محلـه القـلـب وهـو : تسكين الجوارح، أو هما جميعاً. وفي إطلاق النظر إلى موضع السجود شمول المشاهد للكعبة، وقـال الجلال السيوطي في ( الينبوع » : قال « الأوزاعي ) : حكى « المحب الطبري» وجهاً أنه إن كان يشاهد الكعبة، فينظر إليها مع توفر الخشوع واستحسنه، ثم قال: والمذهب النظر إلى موضع سجوده مطلقاً، لأنه لا يأمن ما يلهيه، انتهى (وَ) نظره ) إلى ظَاهِرِ القَدَمِ رَاكِعَاً ، لأنه أدعى إلى الخشوع، :« (۱) (و) نظره (إلى أَرْنَبَةِ أَنْفِهِ سَاجَداً)، لأن تصويب النظر إليها أقرب إلى الخشوع (وإلى حجره جَالِسَاً)؛ لئلا ينظر إلى ما يشغله عما هو فيه من الخشوع استحضاراً لعظمة مولاه، ويكون ملاحظاً قوله : ( اعْبُدِ اللَّهَ كَأَنَّكَ تَرَاهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ تَرَاهُ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَاكَ » (۳). (وَ) نظره ( إلى المَنْكِبَيْن مُسَلَّماً) فينظر إلى أيمنه في الأول، وإلى أيسره في الثاني، لأن المقصود الخشوع، وترك التكلف فإذا تركه صار ناظراً إلى هذه المواضع قصداً، ولم يقصد، وإذا كان في الظلام أو كان بصيراً يلاحظ مؤدى
Chapter on the etiquettes of prayer: The man taking his hands out of his sleeves during the takbir, and the praying person looking at the place of his prostration while standing, at the top of his foot while bowing, at the tip of his nose while prostrating, at his lap while sitting, and at the shoulders while greeting. Chapter on the etiquettes of prayer: We indicated by the partitive 'min' that we did not exhaust all individual etiquettes, but rather mentioned what is available of them. And 'adab' in language is known; al-Jawhari said: 'Adab is discipline of the soul and study; you say: the man is adib (cultured). I taught him manners and he became disciplined.' And in terminology, it is everything the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did once or twice without persisting, like increasing the tasbihat in bowing and prostration, and increasing beyond the prescribed recitation, as in al-'Inaya and al-Diraya and others. And adab is legislated to complete the sunnah, and sunnah to complete the wajib, and wajib to complete the fard, as in al-Bazzaziyya. So from the etiquettes of prayer: (The man taking his hands out of his sleeves during the takbir) i.e., takbirat al-ihram, because it is closer to humility, farther from resembling tyrants, and more conducive to spreading the fingers, except for a necessity like cold and the like. And the woman does not take out her hands, because it leads to uncovering her forearms, which are 'awrah, and her condition is based on concealment; the hermaphrodite is like the woman as a precaution. (And the looking of the praying person) whether man or woman (at the place of his prostration while standing) to protect him from looking at what distracts him from khushu, and we will mention that khushu is in the heart, and it is calming the limbs, or both. And in the absolute looking at the place of prostration, it includes seeing the Ka'bah. Al-Jalal al-Suyuti in al-Yanbu' said: al-Awza'i said: al-Muhibb al-Tabari narrated a view that if one sees the Ka'bah, he looks at it while maintaining khushu, and he approved it. Then he said: The madhhab is to look at the place of prostration absolutely, because he is not safe from distraction. End. (And) his looking (at the top of the foot while bowing), because it is more conducive to khushu. (And) his looking (at the tip of his nose while prostrating), because directing the gaze to it is closer to khushu. (And) his looking (at his lap while sitting), lest he look at what distracts him from khushu, by being mindful of the hadith: 'Worship Allah as if you see Him, for if you do not see Him, indeed He sees you.' (And) his looking (at the shoulders while greeting): he looks at his right shoulder in the first, and at his left in the second, because the purpose is khushu and avoiding affectation; so if he does that, he becomes a looker at these places intentionally but not deliberately. And if he is in darkness or was blind, he observes the meaning.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage defines adab (etiquette) in prayer, distinguishing it from sunnah. Adab in terminology refers to actions the Prophet performed once or twice without regularity, like increasing tasbihat. Adab is intended to perfect sunnah, which perfects wajib, which perfects fard. The specific etiquettes include: (1) For men: taking hands out of sleeves during takbirat al-ihram to show humility and avoid resembling tyrants; this also facilitates spreading fingers. Women do not do so because their forearms are 'awrah and they are required to conceal them; a hermaphrodite follows the woman's rule as a precaution. (2) Looking at the place of prostration while standing directs attention away from distractions. Even if one sees the Ka'bah, the preferred view is to still look at the prostration place. (3) Looking at the top of the foot while bowing enhances humility. (4) Looking at the tip of the nose while prostrating focuses the gaze. (5) Looking at the lap while sitting prevents distraction. (6) Looking at the right shoulder during the first taslim and left during the second, to avoid affectation. These acts are all recommended (sunnah/adab) to cultivate khushu (heartfelt humility).

Key Terms
الأدب (al-adab): Etiquette; actions the Prophet performed once or twice without persistence, legislated to complete the sunnah.
الخشوع (al-khushu): Humility and concentration in prayer; it is in the heart and also manifested by calming the limbs.
التكبير (al-takbir): Here specifically takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir) when entering prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it is not sunnah for women

Key Takeaway
The etiquettes of prayer—where to look and how to position hands—are legislated to perfect the sunnah and cultivate khushu, with specific details for men and women.
